> I take it you're using a 2.5 beta version (you don't say, but that
> message shouldn't occur at all with anything earlier).  If so the issue
> is that error messages are handled by a GSL template, precisely so you
> can customise them.  But for some reason the template cannot be
> processed.
>
> Going out on a limb, I'd say you're probably trying to use Xitami 2.5b1
> or Xitami 2.5b4 NT service (which is actually 2.5b1 in disguise).  Try
> Xitami 2.5b5 (the latest beta) from http://www.xitami.com/

Ok...first newbie issue for me..

ver. 2.5b4
Win98 environment
DSL, dynaminc IP with DNS update, lyksys router, ports to server forward =
and working

Xitami established fine out of the box, web-admin no problem and served =
a site by just dropping the folder into the "webpages" directory.  FTP =
came on fine referring to the standard dirctories and cgi's run fine =
with no issues.  All seems well, let's try the vhost wizzard and see if =
we can offer a user to ftp into the vhost. =20

Check the docs, faq on xitami site, 42 says...=20

-------------------------------------------------------------------------=
-------

42: I want each user to have FTP access to their personal web pages =20

You do not need aliases. Simply assign each user a subdirectory of the =
webpages directory, then specify this directory as their FTP home =
directory (using a full path).=20



-------------------------------------------------------------------------=
-------


I crank up the vhost wizzard and set the FTP root to point absolute to =
the subdirectory "web5", which in turn has been pointed to generate =
under "webpages".  I hit the "create" button and bingo, it's all there.  =
I call up the vhost administrator and can see the references and the =
permissions appear as I would expect.

                            web5 - FTP User Profiles=20

      User name: Password: Login directory: Permissions: Space used =
(Mb): Number of files:=20
      admin admin c:\program files\xitami\webpages\web5/ * 0 0=20
      anonymous  * c:\program files\xitami\webpages\web5/pub/ G 0 0=20
      ftp  * c:\program files\xitami\webpages\web5/pub/ G 0 0=20
      guest    c:\program files\xitami\webpages\web5/guest/ G 0 0=20
      upload  upload c:\program files\xitami\webpages\web5/upload/ P 0 0 =





So I fire up the FTPclient and point to www.XXX.XXX/web5, logging =
admin/admin and I end up at  the FTP root whith Pub, Guest and Upload.

So I try reauthenticating into upload, using upload/upload, send a file, =
hoping it routes to web5, but it lands in upload.

Have I missunderstood what FAQ 42 is trying to tell me?  Can someone =
please embarass me?

OK fine, so I managed to embarrass myself |;-)

I had not followed the FAQ accurately, assuming admin/admin would =
work...oops default admin- not allowed

After writing an individual permission with unique user/pass, no problem

Nice to see that the master host tracks the listing for the sub-hosts =
too, and checks duplications.

Xitami Rocks!

> It's optional.  See the documentation if you want to know what you can
> do with it.

-How- are you opening a "DOS box"? Usually: Start, Run, "command", OK will

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb  1 19:23:48 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 01 Feb 2002 14:23:48 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Perl in a MSDOS box
References: <3C5AE593.9F551E1A@ix.netcom.com>
Message-ID: <3C5AEB44.16DD444A@rci.rutgers.edu>

> After installing xitami server and activeperl I can run scripts ok but I
can't use perl in a dos box to check syntax (perl -c scriptname). I get
a "This Program cannot be run in DOS mode" message.

Also- since you have a web server and Perl on the Win98 machine, you could
stash your Perl script in the cgi-bin folder, open a browser, open
"http://localhost/cgi-bin/doodah.pl", and check functionality. That isn't much
use if you've made a big syntax error though. 

Use this on top of your scripts. If you make a not too big syntax error, this
will try to tell you about it. 

 BEGIN {
 use Env qw(REMOTE_ADDR HTTP_ACCEPT);
 use CGI qw(:standard);
 use CGI::Carp qw(fatalsToBrowser set_message);
 set_message("ooops!");
 };


 -PRR

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (TCD Support)

------Original Message-------

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Date: Tuesday, January 22, 2002 8:28:59 PM
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Subject: [Xitami] Two domain names.

Hello to everyone.

I have had Xitami 2.5b5 running for over a year now and first I must say it
has been a joy to use. Actually all I had to do was install it, made some
html and after that, just forget about it. No need to check every day if my
pages were alive. They truly have been. Including FTP.

I have to agree.  I have, been running Xitami Powered for over 4 years, on a
M$ Operating to say the least! ;-0   I have found over the final OS switch
to a flavor of UNIX, LINUX, xBSD.

I have ADSL connection with static IP. So my
both domains point to same IP-address. Is it possible to make Xitami to
separate these domain names and guide the visitors to sites (in this case
two different folders on same HD) they are looking for or do I have to set
up a DNS-server or something else? I've tried to use virtual hosts but I
just 

Ok here is how I do it and it works, and one thing I have to say before I
tell you is that, it is here at the Xitami Support Forum from great people I
have learned to achieve this.  Another STRONG feature from Imatix! 
-----remember this is just one way to set it up, there are many solutions
and alternatives, I am just telling you the way I have it setup and it works
 

1st:  You have the DSL connection and the Static IP, (The best start you
could ask for), even if you had a block of addresses, it is still better to
bind & multi-home all your Virtual Hosts to one IP, I mean the IP system as
Area codes and phone numbers are running their course.

2nd-Solution-A: Set up a box with FreeBSD (again, there are many available
solutions, I do not want to start a OS war here).  This will be for your
name server.  You will also need 2 more IP's Static for the Name Server. 
Just ask your uplink to provide you with some.  There is rarely a cost
associated with getting more IP's, you just need a valid reason for usage, a
name server is a very valid reason.
!!-This is the most effective solution-!!

2nd-Solution-B:  Have someone do your name server (DNS).  Point of the
matter is, the more control you have of your OWN name server the better. 
There are people that will do it for you, the question is, are they
available to update a name server when ever YOU want, and then at what cost?
If you are interested in this solution, we www.thecomputerdojo.com can
provide this service for you for 9.99 per month.  It is cheaper than buying
another machine and dealing with your uplink trying to get IP's, (some
uplinks charge for extra IP's).

3rd:  Setup a box for Xitami using whatever operating system.  I myself
still run my Xitami Web Server on the M$ Platform.  I am sure some people
will think this is a mistake and would suggest running under some flavor of
UNIX/LINUX.
Bind this machine to the static IP you choose.

4th:  Setup name server with A-Name and C-name, you can do MX resolutions
too, Deerfield 
has a great Mail Daemon   www.mdaemon.com

5th: Now that you have all that setup, the easy part is dealing with Vhosts.
 Here is how you do it.  Go into Xitami Setup, click on Virtual Hosts, click
on NEW:


Create virtual host profile:   .cfg extension is assumed 
stick to the actual domain name, for example: cybercoalition

Overwrite existing?   
ALWAYS!



Select IP address:   All addresses (recommended)209.5.45.142127.0.0.1 
do not change

Or, enter DNS host name:   
here you would put  www.cybercoalition.com




Web page root directory:  
Here you put the path eg: webpages/cybercoalition 
CGI-bin directory:  
best to make separate cgi-bin directories eg:
webpages/cybercoalition/cgi-bin

FTP root directory:  
I use WAR_FTP, was not happy with Xitami's FTP server for what I run.  For a
stand alone webserver FTP it's alright.

Create directories if necessary?  
Absolutely

anything you want

again, up to you.....

anything

and password:  
anything

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb  5 09:28:35 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Mike)
Date: Tue, 5 Feb 2002 01:28:35 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] Linksys Router and Xitami
References: <011301c1ade9$95b4bdc0$6701a8c0@configxp>
Message-ID: <009b01c1ae27$7d4c6240$6501a8c0@ameritech.net>

On my server machine, I had to set my TCP/IP address, host name, domain, dns
primary, secondary and DHCP manually. ( the linksys acquire will usually be
dynamic however) (ADSL)

For one cable client using linksys, we had to follow the linksys help file
for mac address ghosting, which requires a trip to the dos prompt, (assuming
windows), and generate the mac ghost overlay, then input it to linksys.
(motorola cable-modem).  Using the labled mac address from the modem did no
good here. (we could ping but not surf.) This fixed it.

I also forwarded all the noted addresses in the linksys forward page, then
closed up those not needed, as I could disprove them. (make sure your
pointing to the manually configured server ip address for forwarding).  DMZ
was not neccessary nor is it advisable.

If you force a network browser to a full www url, pointing to your page, do
you get out and back in from your own request generation, (that is
www.mypage.whatever as opposed to using the network nnn.nnn.nnn.nnn address?

Maybe do some port scanning from a third party on the net and see what
status is showing up on various ports.

Good luck.
Mike


Anybody have this sort of trouble before? After going to cable from dialup,
using a Linksys router, folks coming in on the internet can get to my FTP,
but not my HTTP.  I can get to my HTTP on the local network. Must be the
router. Have set the IP the Xitami server is on to DMZ, as well as added
forwarding for this IP for ports 21, 80 and 81. No go.


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb  5 07:28:05 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jeff Hamblin)
Date: Mon, 4 Feb 2002 23:28:05 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] Linksys Router and Xitami
References: <011301c1ade9$95b4bdc0$6701a8c0@configxp>
Message-ID: <005b01c1ae16$d198a540$9f00a8c0@ziggy>

Most cable ISPs are now blocking port 80 incoming, but not FTP (21). So
you'll need to change your port base for HTTP.

BTW, if you've set the computer running Xitami as DMZ it is wide open, and
you don't need to, and shouldn't, forward any ports to it. DMZ means all
incoming requests are directed to DMZ IP address.

As the other responder mentioned, a DMZ setup is inadvisable. Better to not
use DMZ and just forward the necessary incoming ports to the Xitami
machine's IP address.

-Jeff

References: <011301c1ade9$95b4bdc0$6701a8c0@configxp> <009b01c1ae27$7d4c6240$6501a8c0@ameritech.net> <015f01c1ae49$3047ebf0$6701a8c0@configxp>
Message-ID: <010b01c1ae72$5a797aa0$6501a8c0@ameritech.net>

Mike,

You can go to the Linksys website http://www.linksys.com "services and
support", "knowledge base" and search for "mac address clone"

Basically, you run "winipcfg" from the start/run menu (on the server) and
you will see you your ip config data.  Select the dropdown to point to the
card your accessing by, and you should see the "adapter address" listed
first.  Write that 12 digit number down. (if your running NT, you'll need to
go dos prompt and type "winipcfg /all"

Now, call up the Linksys and go to the "setup" area  see where it says WAN
IP address?  Write that down in case you have to revert.  Now select the
"advanced" tab then the "mac addr clone" tab.  Type in the 12 digit from the
winipcfg session and confirm it.  When you call up the setup tab again, you
should see the hardware address of the netcard as the wan ip address.  You
may have to do a reset on the router, I'm not sure.

Root around on linksys' web sight and be patient.  Work through logically
and use "ping" to tell you if your getting through at all.

Mike

    I have an internal Mandrake/Apache behind a Linksys. No DMZ, just port
forwarding (port 80).

    I also use www.dhs.org to have a symbolic name that I can give to
people, which points to my Linksys IP. So, when they use http://.... it will
go to my internal Linux.

    Of course the symbolic name does not work internally (intranet) because
it will point to teh Linksys, and I end up in teh Linksys admin. So, it will
only work from teh outside. Internally I use teh IP http://192.168.3.200

    I never cfg'ed DNS etc.

marcio

Thanks Paul,

"/Admin" and "/Setup" are both created as protected uri's in 2.5 vhost
wizard and the docs seem to suggest that /setup will provide a "limited" vh
wba, whereby vhosted clients can make "limited" setup changes to their own
accounts remotely, using the xitami interface.  This is obviously an
attractive feature to be able to offer to vhost clients, as well as a
marketing tool for those of us who would wish to propel clients into a
commercial relationship with Xitami, where we would demo the product and
move them to purchase from Xitami and assist them under our deployment.

Every time I try to reference the url, either internally or externally, even
by way of  "host@" under http/1.1, I end up at the Xitami default page, as
if I need to have a local DNS "host" record for the vhost url to access, to
get to the vhost "/setup" realm.  When I try to access the vhost via the
"/admin", I end up in the admin realm, but the only authorization it
recognizes is my own Xitami master host permission.

Are there no users utilizing this convention or am I simply misunderstanding
the application of it, or is it not implemented yet?

You are the first to even try to respond to the many references I've left in
the archive, regarding this endeavor.  Thank you for responding Paul.



Is this perhaps a new convention to xitami which is not yet full
implemented?

> If 2.5 is different, sorry for the interruption.

They do not specifically block port 80. They will not provide support and if
they find out (by means of a complaint) they will require you to get a
business account.

A friend of mine was running a mail server and forgot to block relaying and
got busted by RR and they required him to get the upgraded account.

I am having a similiar problem except I can get some traffic through and
some cannot get through. Certain people can get on anytime they want and
certain people cannot ever get on. At the same time.

At first I thought it was Earthlink DSL but they do not block port 80. They
do not prohibit running a website but do not support it in any fashion
except for the original hookup.

I setup a laptop and tested it from home. The certain people could not get
on. I took the laptop over to a friends house with RR and it worked like a
charm.

Still can't figure out what is the problem at home.

Mike,

In looking at RR terms, I found this: "You are prohibited from excessive
consumption of resources, including CPU time, memory, disk space and session
time. You may not use resource-intensive programs, which negatively impact
other customers or the performance of Road Runner systems or networks. Road
Runner reserves the right to terminate or limit such activities."

They don't specifically say they block port 80, but..
The commercial accounts that they talk about not allowing are on the user's
personal page that is on their servers.

    Anyone can check connectivity online. You just need a Java-enabled
browser.

1) Go to http://www.visualware.com/visualroute/index.html

2) Click on Live Demo

3) Select a server (USA, Virginia works for me)

4) Enter the target URL or host name or IP.


    You can also click on SNAP on teh applet to open a TXT window with the
results, which I pasted below.

marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb  5 23:47:28 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Mike McDaniel)
Date: Tue, 5 Feb 2002 18:47:28 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Linksys Router and Xitami HTTP RESOLVED
Message-ID: <005001c1ae9f$7871c6c0$6701a8c0@configxp>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_004D_01C1AE75.8F4190D0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

Thanks for everyone's support.  Many good thinks came out of this =
thread, and I must give credit to Jeff Hamplin for the final winning =
moves. He said to resolve the situation where an ISP is blocking port 80 =
(and they are at some RR locations, not all) the thing that's needed is =
to first set the base port for Xitami's HTTP to 9000. This will in =
effect make the port for HTTP be 9080 as Xitami adds 80 to your entry in =
that field. Notice it is by default a 0. Then add a forward to the =
router for 9080. Lastly, FTP always worked right from the start as RR =
was not blocking that. However when you tell Xitami to use 9000, you are =
also without knowing it telling Xitami the FTP port is 9021. You can =
enter an FTP port of -8979 to put your FTP port back to 21 and keep web =
at 9080. This is done by manually editing the Xitami default.cfg file =
and adding an entry:

[FTP]
   Port=3D-8979

That should be -8979  -- a negative number. 9000-8979=3D21


Thus users will still be able to access FTP the usual way, however for =
HTTP there is the requirement now to add the port to the URL

http://mikemcdaniel.dynu.com:9080

ftp://mikemcdaniel.dynu.com

Again, thanks for everyone's help.=20







------=_NextPart_000_004D_01C1AE75.8F4190D0

    Anyone can check connectivity online. You just need a Java-enabled
browser.
 
1) Go to http://www.visualware.com/visualroute/index.html
 
2) Click on Live Demo
 
3) Select a server (USA, Virginia works for me)
 
4) Enter the target URL or host name or IP.
 
 
    You can also click on SNAP on teh applet to open a TXT window with
the results, which I pasted below.
 
marcio

    Anyone can check connectivity online. You just need a Java-enabled
browser.

1) Go to http://www.visualware.com/visualroute/index.html

2) Click on Live Demo

3) Select a server (USA, Virginia works for me)

4) Enter the target URL or host name or IP.


    You can also click on SNAP on teh applet to open a TXT window with the
results, which I pasted below.

marcio

    Anyone can check connectivity online. You just need a Java-enabled
browser.
 
1) Go to http://www.visualware.com/visualroute/index.html
 
2) Click on Live Demo
 
3) Select a server (USA, Virginia works for me)
 
4) Enter the target URL or host name or IP.
 
 
    You can also click on SNAP on teh applet to open a TXT window with
the results, which I pasted below.
 
marcio

From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org

    Anyone can check connectivity online. You just need a Java-enabled
browser.
 
1) Go to http://www.visualware.com/visualroute/index.html
 
2) Click on Live Demo
 
3) Select a server (USA, Virginia works for me)
 
4) Enter the target URL or host name or IP.
 
 
    You can also click on SNAP on teh applet to open a TXT window with
the results, which I pasted below.
 
marcio

Could folks please adjust their posting habits?  This particular post was
over 27kB in length, and yet actually had much less than 1kB of new
content.  The rest was needlessly-repeated, many-times-previously-quoted
stuff, and then the whole bloody caboodle all over again in HTML (which
made that traceroute table "interesting", since each line of it resulted
in hundreds of bytes of &nbsp; sequences etc.).

<http://www.geocities.com/nnqweb/nquote.html>, whilst written with
newsgroup postings in mind, is equally applicable to the traffic on a
mailing list.

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)

In message <46880@dsl.co.uk>, Brian {Hamilton Kelly} writes:
>In message <00b201c1ae9b$8f9e88a0$0100a8c0@celeron2k> "Marcio Marchini" writes:
>>     Anyone can check connectivity online. You just need a Java-enabled
>> browser.
>
>Could folks please adjust their posting habits?  This particular post was
>over 27kB in length, and yet actually had much less than 1kB of new
>content.  [much repeated quoted text]

The mailing list currently rejects posts bigger than 30KB in size.  In
view of the excessive quoting that is going on, I'm tempted to reduce
this even further.  Can anyone think of a good reason for allowing posts
bigger than 10KB?  (The 30KB was set to allow people to include
configuration examples; but generally they're best done as smaller
snippets anyway.)

Anyone who is actually seeking an answer should note that I pretty much
ignore anything with more than one or two levels of quoting out of hand;
the rest goes into my "to be answered when I get time" pile, and stays
there until either (a) someone else answers it or (b) I get time.

Trimming quotes to only the most appropriate portions is
_strongly_encouraged_.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org

In message <46880@dsl.co.uk>, Brian {Hamilton Kelly} writes:
>In message <00b201c1ae9b$8f9e88a0$0100a8c0@celeron2k> "Marcio Marchini"

>writes:
>>     Anyone can check connectivity online. You just need a 
>> Java-enabled browser.
>
>Could folks please adjust their posting habits?  This particular post 
>was over 27kB in length, and yet actually had much less than 1kB of new

>content.  [much repeated quoted text]

The mailing list currently rejects posts bigger than 30KB in size.  In
view of the excessive quoting that is going on, I'm tempted to reduce
this even further.  Can anyone think of a good reason for allowing posts
bigger than 10KB?  (The 30KB was set to allow people to include
configuration examples; but generally they're best done as smaller
snippets anyway.)

Anyone who is actually seeking an answer should note that I pretty much
ignore anything with more than one or two levels of quoting out of hand;
the rest goes into my "to be answered when I get time" pile, and stays
there until either (a) someone else answers it or (b) I get time.

Trimming quotes to only the most appropriate portions is
_strongly_encouraged_.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

--
Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami

How do you know what port 80 is blocked when is says Analysis: IP
packets are being lost past network "AT&T ITS" at hop 13. There is
insufficient cached 
information to determine the next network at hop 14.

 -----Original Message-----
Anybody have this sort of trouble before? After going to cable from
dialup, using a Linksys router, folks coming in on the internet can get
to my FTP, but not my HTTP.  I can get to my HTTP on the local network.
Must be the router. Have set the IP the Xitami server is on to DMZ, as
well as added forwarding for this IP for ports 21, 80 and 81. No go.

Port 80 has simply been blocked on your cable network.  I've had the same
problem.  I pulled my hair out trying to figure it out until I finally
forced tech support to admit the blockage.  Blocking port 80 have become
common since the introduction of the code red type virus's that cripple ISP
bandwidth's.  Try using port 8080......

 > I just contacted RoadRunner and they said, no they don't block port
80, but residential accounts don't permit web servers. So, don't know if
I'm getting the straight answer or not. Can't tell if I should beleive
them or not. 
 
I just noticed this post. I went through this myself recently. Road
Runner as a company doesn't block port 80 but in some areas the local
cable connector company might. As far as web servers being prohibited on
RR, I have heard them say it is not allowed but have been unsuccessful
in locating any place in their agreement that says so. 
 
I have Cox Cable in Fairfax County, Northern Virginia just outside
Washington DC. In some areas of the county (including mine) port 80 is
blocked because they were having system overloads from that Code Red
problem last summer. Other parts of the county it is not blocked. I have
several Xitami servers running in friends homes around the county. I
have given up on using port 80 and use 443. My  DNS forwarding service (
http://www.dns2go.com ) gives you the ability to change the port of a
domain preceded with the www. I think that the Xitami service also
allows this but am not sure. Hope this gives some more info.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb  6 03:21:07 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Tue, 5 Feb 2002 22:21:07 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Linksys Router and Xitami

Message-ID: <000601c1aebd$50f24070$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

> The mailing list currently rejects posts bigger than 30KB in size.


	An HTML MIME message comes in an alternate envelope which also includes the TXT
piece. One possible workaround is to extract the first TXT piece and throw away
HTML's. This way HTML e-mail is automatically discarded, and just the txt part
survives.

	Maybe listservers have this option already ?

	The problem is when e-mail starts in HTML, then replies will probably come in
HTML too. And in these cases it can be hard to clip pieces, depending on your
e-mail program.

	Plain TXT e-mail should be fine for this list.

marcio


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb  6 08:38:42 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Mike)

Ya know, watching the threads that are running here, leaves me shaking my
head.

List operators have the ability to obtain an agreement from those who would
join and take a responsible direction toward educating their users, in
support of the product base their working to expand.  This, as opposed to
open or direct dialog which serves to show their public flames, brow beating
and criticizm, from those who moderate the service and supposedly are there
to propel the product's growth and help the users.

A service can easily automate moderation criteria and react with warnings,
education and even soft or hard ban's on users who fail to comply, without
ever taxing the moderation group, other than to establish it initially.
Even teenagers have been able to handle the concept in ICQ and other public
forums.

If the list group were to sponser a venue for users to have online
interaction, they could provide a forum for off-topic dialog which could
work to Xitami's benefit, strengthening their shareware base and evolving
into commercial sales.  As well, the technology could be an implementation
to Xitami, further touting it's already robust package.

I've been tempted to introduce the product into my customer base, because of
the ease of use and bredth of capability, however the exposure I continue to
see here, tells me those opportunities will have to wait awhile.  I'm sure
someone would gladly tell me "If you spend the money for a registration,
you'll get quality support."  I'm not conviced by what I'm seeing here and
those of us in sales understand it reflects on the corporate mentality as a
whole.  As well, we in shareware work hard, are patient and at times take
risks to help others develop a good product.  Consider these things
gentlemen, even if mid-scale integration is your bread and butter, this
server product has a strong potential, worth the professionalism of you who
develop it and those who apply it.  Your competition is probably having a
field day showing this list to customers.

If I'm over quota, would someone dig this out of the technical consultant's
bit bucket? {:-(

I'll get off my soap box now, thank you for your time.
Mike Wilson

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb  6 06:28:42 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Wed, 06 Feb 2002 07:28:42 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Linksys Router and Xitami
Message-ID: <46886@dsl.co.uk>

In message <200202060143.OAA20886@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
   Ewen McNeill writes:

> The mailing list currently rejects posts bigger than 30KB in size.  In
> view of the excessive quoting that is going on, I'm tempted to reduce
> this even further.  Can anyone think of a good reason for allowing posts
> bigger than 10KB?  (The 30KB was set to allow people to include
> configuration examples; but generally they're best done as smaller
> snippets anyway.)

Whilst being a strong opponent of over-quoting, I don't believe there
should be any automatic restriction based on size (although obviously the
list doesn't want to be propagating the binary photograph of the poster's
dog that someone thoughtlessly attaches to their post).

What IS needed is some PERSONAL discipline on the part of some of the
posters: perhaps it is just that they've only ever used e-mail in the
context of an intra-office memo (at Ethernet speeds) --- they just "hit
reply", and then do nothing about trimming the quoted material, but leave
it in one congealing lump after their (sometimes few) words of wisdom.  

There really is NO need to quote the entirety of all the previous
messages in the thread. There is even less necessity to quote them all
underneath, totally out of context, especially when no one can see,
without a lot of guesswork and scrolling back and forth, just what "you
need to change the oojimaflip" implies.

Quote JUST enough to establish a context for your reply; if the reply is
just a single point, then cut out EVERYTHING apart from that point, and
put the quote UNDERNEATH it.  If replying to multiple points, do so one
at a time.  Configure your mailer so that it quotes previous messages in
this sort of style, with a "> " at the beginning of each line and an
attribution ("On such-and-such a date, so-and-so said:") above the quoted
text.

Oh, and DO quote SOMETHING; posts on a mailing list can arrive seriously
out of order, and often without the "clues" to thread them into context
automatically.

> Anyone who is actually seeking an answer should note that I pretty much
> ignore anything with more than one or two levels of quoting out of hand;

Sometimes it is necessary to retain some more levels (say where one
poster is refuting the answer given by one or two others to some original
question) but in general that is correct: one doesn't need the WHOLE
provenance of the question and the arguments.

When cutting out older material, ensure that the attribution is correct:
people get somewhat miffed if it's written that they said something that
they never had any hand in.

> the rest goes into my "to be answered when I get time" pile, and stays
> there until either (a) someone else answers it or (b) I get time.

Over-quoters please note the above: you are less likely to get a reply
from the very person with the greatest knowledge.  This will tend to
apply to other knowledgable people as well: they might not have time to
reconstruct the poster's thoughts out of the mess that is the stream-of-
consciousness in a big thread.

> Trimming quotes to only the most appropriate portions is
> _strongly_encouraged_.

Hear, hear.

The page <http://www.geocities.com/nnqweb/nquote.html> provides plenty
of justification for that point, and for the other matters I've raised.

The only other point is this nonsense of people writing in HTML.
Unfortunately, they often are blissfully unaware that it's happening.
Outlook Express and all the other "mailers" include a setting to
suppress this infelicity: sadly in some issues of the programs, the
default is to post in both ASCII and HTML.  That format can sometimes be
triggered when replying to such a message, under the control of another
setting.

If you can reject posts based on size, could you not do the same where
there's a "Content: multipart/alternative" in the MIME headers?

-- 
Brian {Hamilton Kelly}                                          bhk@dsl.co.uk
    "We have gone from a world of concentrated knowledge and wisdom to one of
    distributed ignorance.  And we know and understand less while being incr-
    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs

To the list operators: maybe it will be a better alternative to use some 
sort of bulletin board (ultiboard is a good one) for postings. (example:

attach documents, difficult to quote and edit text, ...) but after a while 
i began to appreciate the board.

you can check the board whenever you want, not when you check your mail.

windows/unix/mac/...

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_006F_01C1AF05.63337AE0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

>I just contacted RoadRunner and they said, no they don't block port 80, =
but residential accounts don't permit web servers. >So, don't know if =
I'm getting the straight answer or not. Can't tell if I should beleive =
them or not.



I am also on Road Runner (Central Florida).  They told me they block =
port 80 nationwide.  I was never able to get port 80 to work.  =
Fortunately the tech I spoke with also runs a server from his home, and =
told me it could be done which made me persistant enough to find =
available ports.

I use dns2go ( www.dns2go.com - its free) handle my dynamic ip adress.  =
In the dns2go client, under the Service Settings tab, I checked =
"Redirect web requests (with a www prefix)" and picked "To my current IP =
address ont port:" and set it to 6080.

Then I edited my defaults.cfg file in my xitami directory to say:

#  Created at installation time
#
!  Loading defaults.cfg file...
[Server]
priority=3D1
portbase=3D6000
background=3D1
[FTP]
port=3D-5979
dataport=3D5800
user-file=3Dftpusers.aut
directory-file=3Dftpdirs.aut
[Security]
filename=3Ddefaults.aut

[Filter]
-php=3Dc:\PHP\php.exe

The stuff that matters is:

[Server]
portbase=3D6000  This sets the web server port to 6080 which is where =
dns2go directs it.

[FTP]
port=3D-5979    This brings the FTP server port back down to 21 (make =
sure to use -5979) as portbase is an offset (+80) for all ports
data-port=3D5800  this is actually a mistake, but it works for now.  I =
shoulda used -5800 cause my intent was to bring the FTP data port down =
to 200.  I have issues where some people have trouble connecting with =
FTP client software, but everyone can connect and log-in with IE, so I =
leave it alone out of laziness.  I found out later that xitami being set =
to data-port 200 was actually a type-o in the xitami.cfg file in my =
particular release.  It should start at 20.  So this should actually be =
set to -5980, then it should work with all FTP clients.

What this does:
dns2go forwards all www prefixed web requests to port 6080 so my url is =
still www.mydomain.com but, since www.prefixes are forwarded to that =
port my FTP address is just ftp://mydomin.com=20

I really don't think you are ever gonna get port 80 to work on Road =
Runner. =20

I also set up www.mydomain.dns2go.com (which is free too) to get =
everything working until all the dns servers pointed to dns2go so that =
www.mydomain.com would work.

Good Luck,

Jay Aldrich

My Outlook has always been and always will be set up to send in plain text.
Unfortunately, Outlook automatically responds to a html message with html.
I do not think there is a way to change it, other than to change the format
of each reply itself before you send it, as outlooks assumes that by
replying to an html-formatted email, it is replying to an html
preferred/capable email client.  Outlook also does not let you know if an
email is formatted in plain text or html unless you check the emails
properties or specifically check the email make sure that > symbols are in
front of the senders original post or it has bars in front of it.

I apologize in advance, but I will surely find it difficult to remember to
check each email's format before I reply to it.  I can however promise that
no html formatted emails will originate from me.

No, I've seen it too. For those PHP packages that I really wanted to work

To the list operators: maybe it will be a better alternative to use some

sort of bulletin board (ultiboard is a good one) for postings. (example:

http://www.powerbasic.com/support/forums/Ultimate.cgi). I once created
such 
a bulletin board and it's easy to maintain.

Your mailbox is not flooded with mails you probably won't read, the
threads 
are separated by subject.
When i first used a bulletin board, i didn't like the idea (impossible
to 
attach documents, difficult to quote and edit text, ...) but after a
while 
i began to appreciate the board.
You can get a notification whenever somebody respond to your posting and

you can check the board whenever you want, not when you check your mail.
And you can create different forums for those who only work with 
windows/unix/mac/...

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb  6 20:31:52 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Wed, 06 Feb 2002 15:31:52 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] $php_self with php4
References: <LKBBKLDHICNIAKJMKNCEAEBCDMAA.warren@warrenernst.com>
Message-ID: <3C6192B8.190878F8@2cah.com>

Warren 'Llama' Ernst wrote:
> 
> No, I've seen it too. For those PHP packages that I really wanted to work
> that uses $php_self, someone else figured out what the package wanted for
> this variable, and then I set it manually as a non-system variable in the
> packages configuration file, such as:

FYI, after doing a lot of research and reading numerous posts from the PHP-DEV
list.

This is not a problem that is specific to Xitami. It occurs when PHP is run as
a CGI process, which is how we use PHP with Xitami.

The solution is, as Warren pointed out, to explicity set $PHP_SELF. If the PHP
scripts are written in a modular fashion this is easy, but if they aren't it
can be a pain.

-- 

Craig Morrison
  http://www.mtsprofessional.com/
  A Win32 Email server that works for you.

Date: Wed, 6 Feb 2002 15:46:10 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Is this exploitable? Switch to bulletin board-mode?
In-Reply-To: <001e01c1af4c$bd957af0$972de00c@personal>

	Or a Newsgroup. People can use their NNTP clients (I use XNews
http://xnews.3dnews.net/), and there's even some web interfaces for NNTP
newsgroups available, for those who love a pure web browser solution.

	You can see Threading properly, etc.

	Most good News readers actually warn you if you try to reply including the
entire original message.

	XNews can also color included paragraphs differently, so it's easy to make
sense out of the ">", ">>", ">>>"and so on. All while keeping messages in pure
TXT, no HTML.

	Just an idea...

marcio

Warren 'Llama' Ernst wrote:
> 
> Is there ANY solution to be found? Is there any alternative to running PHP
> as a CGI process for Windows Xitami?

Considering the ISAPI/SAPI version of PHP is still not considered stable, no.

The alternative is to use PHP as a module with (dare I say it) Apache, but
that defeats the purpose of using our lean, clean and mean Xitami setups.

Indeed; and this post of yours was correctly in that format.

> Unfortunately, Outlook automatically responds to a html message with html.
> I do not think there is a way to change it, other than to change the format
> of each reply itself before you send it, as outlooks assumes that by
> replying to an html-formatted email, it is replying to an html

Amazed though I am to hear this, I've just looked at my partner's machine
(she uses Outlook 2000 as a mail client, fetching her mail from this OS/2
machine using POP3, and sending her outgoing mail to the SMTP server
hereon), and indeed I cannot find anything that deals with what to do in
that event.

Netscape has an option "always send in plain ASCII, even when the
original is in HTML (or multipart/alternative)".  Whilst astounded by
MICROS~1 non-provision of an option to suppress HTML altogether, I am not
completely surprised.

All the same, it might be worth asking if there might be a setting after
all on the <news:microsoft.public.outlook.configuration> froup.

In the meantime, I'll try to remember to be less scathing of those using
Outlook [Express] (although, of course, one has to question the wisdom of
using a piece of software that has been demonstrated to commit over 200
violations of Internet standards (as enshrined in various RFCs).

> I checked the format of this response before I sent it, and according to
> Outlook it is plain text before it left me.

Yep: it's fine.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb  6 20:15:03 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Wed, 06 Feb 2002 21:15:03 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Is this exploitable? Switch to bulletin board-mode?
Message-ID: <46893@dsl.co.uk>

In message <001e01c1af4c$bd957af0$972de00c@personal>
   "Many Lists" writes:

> How about a list option of digest mode? It works in other places.  I
> filter my e-mail in outlook into folders and use a separate e-mail just
> for lists rather than use my personal e-mail so when I check my mail
> remotely through a web interface I am not flooded with stuff I don't
> need to reply to.

Good idea.

> My opinion. I hate web based forums.  I was on one for awhile at Winamp
> trying to get a streaming audio server online, but sometimes you like to
> have more information rather than when you just post.  In the e-mail if
> you don't like the 
> Thread you just delete the whole thread.

Hmm, I've never used a mailer that has the capability of deleting traffic
on a "thread" that has not yet arrived.  How do you ensure that mail is
threaded anyway, given that the use of In-Reply-To is only sketchily
followed by some MUAs, and that others use References instead, which is
something that actually belongs to Usenet?  (RFC-2822, which is still
only a "proposed standard", mentions References for the first time; it
was not part of THE standard RFC-822.  Moreover, the latter never
mandated the use of I-R-T, and even the new one only places both at the
level of a SHOULD, and not a MUST.)

Perhaps the amount of traffic on this list could justify a proper Usenet
newsgroup.  Perhaps a case could be made for restructuring the
comp.infosystems.www.servers.* hierarchy, which (foolishly, IMHO)
contains the groups:
    comp.infosystems.www.servers.mac
    comp.infosystems.www.servers.misc
    comp.infosystems.www.servers.ms-windows
    comp.infosystems.www.servers.unix

Obviously no one envisaged the concept of a cross-platform server; all
the same comp.infosystems.www.servers.xitami might not be beyond the
realms of possibility.

Would anyone care to try raising an RFD?

(OTOH, Imatix could run an NNTP server on their systems, that handles
only a xitami newsgroup, or hierarchy of them.  I'm generally against the
concept of special-to-one-server-only newsgroups, since I consider that
the advantage of a newsgroup is that one reads it from the most local
server, wherever one happens to be.  But Borland use one, as do Serenity
Systems (for the ecomstation.* hierarchy).)

In message <46893@dsl.co.uk>, Brian {Hamilton Kelly} writes:
>Perhaps the amount of traffic on this list could justify a proper Usenet
>newsgroup.  

This is probably true.  (And I like newsgroups much more than I like web
"message boards", and to some extent more than I like mailing lists.)

>Perhaps a case could be made for restructuring the 
>comp.infosystems.www.servers.* hierarchy [....]
>Would anyone care to try raising an RFD?

If anyone wants to follow this through (start the RFD process for a new
newsgroup), then I'm happy to provide some support (eg, statistics on
number of users of the mailing list, etc).  However I don't have time to
do it myself.

Anyone keen to see about establishing a newsgroup?  (Possibly even an
alt.* newsgroup would do.)

>(OTOH, Imatix could run an NNTP server on their systems, that handles
>only a xitami newsgroup, or hierarchy of them.  

This is generally the worst-of-all-worlds.  The major advantage of
newsgroups is that they're well distributed.  And if there's just one
newsserver carrying the newsgroup, then everyone has to adjust their
newsservers to read from that one.  It's basically a web "message board"
with different software.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Hello...

http://test.modernwonder.com  & www.modernwonder.com are two different
servers one in in Oregon and the other in in Kansas. The company I
register my domain offers free dns so I donts need to us dnstogo  but I
may try it. The company I have my domain name registered through
operates the DNS server, so any changes I make as in the addition of an
alias or the location of the main web are reflected instantly. In the
case of modernwonder.com I have that set for url forwarding to another
domain. This is for my father in law.  Test is my server for devlopement
purposes. I host everything of mine on a cold fusion server. I really
want ot get into Cold fusion so I rent space out of a server in Kasas> I
host a few sites on there already. I have about 4-6 Gb worth of
transfers per month.  This seemed to be the most ecconomical way to do
it right now.

Again when I changed the portbase it was reflected in the control panel
and I was only able to connect using the port number I specified so I
know the cfg is correct.

Www is not needed on any domain.  Most ISP set up the dns or the
webserver to default to www. This is called a domain alias.

Talked to ATT today.  I am also having troubles sending files via icq
too. They claim to only filter ports: 137, 138, 139, 520 and 1080.
Wonder why... I have tried other port numbers like 6080 and higher ones
as well. Still no effect.

As for my posts that I get back form the list, all say Plain Text at the
top.  I will send the e-mail to you with a screenshot.  I hope that this
will end that discussion.

Thanks
-----Original Message-----
From: Control-Freak [mailto:control-freak@cfl.rr.com] 
Sent: Wednesday, February 06, 2002 1:25 PM
To: Many Lists
Subject: Re: [Xitami] Linksys Router and Xitami


MessageHello Many Lists,

> I have the exact same setup as you but it wont work for me.
> http://test.modernwonder.com/   If I type the name in it comes up for
me,
> but it does not for my wife at work. Could you please check it?

I was not able to connect to http://test.modernwonder.com  but, I was
able to connect to www.modernwonder.com .

Personally, I have never tried to use subdomains in this setup yet,
although I will soon.  But, there are a few points to look at here
regardless.  So . . .

A) if you are using dns2go to port forward for you, notice that it only
forwards web requests with the www prefix.  So the URL
http://test.modernwonder.com will not port forward.  Dns2go will instead
try to send it to your ip on port 80 regardles of what you have it set
to in the client.

B) when someone tries to connect to you from near within the Road Runner
network, dns2go forwards them directly to your IP, so actually they end
up contacting you from within the Road Runner network and may not
encounter a port 80 block on their way.  We are probably far enough
apart that I still encounter a port 80 block on my way to you - so i do
not see your site.

C) when you use vhosting on xitami, you get a separate defaults.cfg file
for each one.  If this one is set to a portbase of 0, it is listening on
port 80 anyway.  If it has a higher portbase, you probably wouldn't be
able to connect to it because dns2go is not forwarding since there is no
www prefix.

Here's what I would try:
1) Change your vhost to www.test.modernwonder.com
2) Check the defaults.cfg in the folder that xitami creates.  Make sure
to set the portbase to 6000 or 8000 or whatever it is that works for
www.modernwonder.com .
3) go ahead and register www.test.modernwonder.com at dns2go in the
multi-domain manager section of the site, and make sure it is "grouped"
with www.modernwonder.com .  I'm not sure if the www is required, but
you should at least register test.modernwonder.com.
4) wait about a day for things to sort themselves out . . .

Hopefully that helps, if not, let me know and I will play around some
here.

Jay Steven Aldrich

P.S. Thanks for the global outlook reply setting, Jeff Hamblin.  And
sorry Many Lists, but it seems you are still sending in html.

Trust me this is not a lot of posts for an e-mail discussion group!   I
get over 300+ a day in www.isp-wireless.com along! As for newsgroups it
seems for the most part that us techies are the only ones that use them.
Less ISP's (from what I read on the isp lists) are supporting them due
to the fact that people don't use them much like the free webspace they
get.  The following was a post on the list.

"I run a small ISP here in Oklahoma, we offer it because with our Linux
server once we place them on our server they automatically get a home
page. I have only had 3 people use it out of 400 users..."

So ISP's are either outsourcing because not as many people request them
or use them along with shell accounts, webpage space and newsgroups.
Form the Isp standpoint Newsgroups take a lot of resources. Money,
hundreds of gigs worth of space...

-----Original Message-----
From: Control-Freak [mailto:control-freak@cfl.rr.com] 
Sent: Wednesday, February 06, 2002 1:25 PM
To: Many Lists
Subject: Re: [Xitami] Linksys Router and Xitami


MessageHello Many Lists,

> I have the exact same setup as you but it wont work for me.
> http://test.modernwonder.com/ <http://test.modernwonder.com/%A0%A0>
If I type the name in it comes up for
me,
> but it does not for my wife at work. Could you please check it?

I was not able to connect to http://test.modernwonder.com
<http://test.modernwonder.com /> but, I was
able to connect to www.modernwonder.com <http://www.modernwonder.com/>
.

Personally, I have never tried to use subdomains in this setup yet,
although I will soon.  But, there are a few points to look at here
regardless.  So . . .

A) if you are using dns2go to port forward for you, notice that it only
forwards web requests with the www prefix.  So the URL
http://test.modernwonder.com <http://test.modernwonder.com/>  will not
port forward.  Dns2go will instead
try to send it to your ip on port 80 regardles of what you have it set
to in the client.

B) when someone tries to connect to you from near within the Road Runner
network, dns2go forwards them directly to your IP, so actually they end
up contacting you from within the Road Runner network and may not
encounter a port 80 block on their way.  We are probably far enough
apart that I still encounter a port 80 block on my way to you - so i do
not see your site.

C) when you use vhosting on xitami, you get a separate defaults.cfg file
for each one.  If this one is set to a portbase of 0, it is listening on
port 80 anyway.  If it has a higher portbase, you probably wouldn't be
able to connect to it because dns2go is not forwarding since there is no
www prefix.

Here's what I would try:
1) Change your vhost to www.test.modernwonder.com
<http://www.test.modernwonder.com/> 
2) Check the defaults.cfg in the folder that xitami creates.  Make sure
to set the portbase to 6000 or 8000 or whatever it is that works for
www.modernwonder.com <http://www.modernwonder.com/>  .
3) go ahead and register www.test.modernwonder.com
<http://www.test.modernwonder.com/>  at dns2go in the
multi-domain manager section of the site, and make sure it is "grouped"
with www.modernwonder.com <http://www.modernwonder.com/>  .  I'm not
sure if the www is required, but
you should at least register test.modernwonder.com.
4) wait about a day for things to sort themselves out . . .

Hopefully that helps, if not, let me know and I will play around some
here.

Jay Steven Aldrich

P.S. Thanks for the global outlook reply setting, Jeff Hamblin.  And
sorry Many Lists, but it seems you are still sending in html.

In-Reply-To: <200202062156.KAA27598@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <003301c1af68$68c44f80$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

> >(OTOH, Imatix could run an NNTP server on their systems, that handles
> >only a xitami newsgroup, or hierarchy of them.


	Yes. I actually use the newsgroups by VMware news.vmware.com , by Creative Labs
news.creative.com, the Eclipse one news.eclipse.org and the HTML-Kit one
chamisplace.com.


> This is generally the worst-of-all-worlds.  The major advantage of
> newsgroups is that they're well distributed.  And if there's just one
> newsserver carrying the newsgroup, then everyone has to adjust their
> newsservers to read from that one.  It's basically a web "message board"
> with different software.


	No need to adjust newsservers. You just adjust your newsclient to have an extra
profile/account, to use that specific server instead of teh one in your ISP.

	No need to vote or anything. You can just install your own NNTP server with
your own groups. Lots of people operate that way. Including, as I said, Creative
Labs, IBM, VMware, Microsoft, etc.

marcio


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb  6 23:54:09 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Control-Freak)
Date: Wed, 6 Feb 2002 18:54:09 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Linksys Router and Xitami
References: <00d801c1af54$cb15c600$b61e2341@concentric.net> <5.1.0.14.0.20020206173114.00a57ba0@66.70.205.209>
Message-ID: <015701c1af69$928b15a0$b61e2341@concentric.net>

Hello Many Lists,

I'm sorry, but I thought you said:

> > > I have the exact same setup as you but it wont work for me.

1) You are not using Road Runner - you are using AT&T
2) You are not using dns2go, you are using some other name server
3) You are using a subdomain of a domain that is hosted in another state - I
have a single domain
4) Doesn't sound like your ip is dynamic, although it is not clear at this
point
5) You are using the xitami html interface,  while I am editing the config
files directly

The suggestions I gave in my last post was specific to my setup.  And, yes,
www is required in order to use port forwarding in dns2go.  I know it is not
required in general, but it is what the dns2go sever program specifically
looks for in order to know what to port forward and not port forward.  In
other words dns2go will not port forward http://mydomain.com  , but it will
port forward http://www.mydomain.com .  It all ends up at the same ip, but
only the one with the www prefix gets port forwarded by dns2go (in other
words its specific to dns2go).

I'm sorry but your setup is very different than mine.  From your responses,
it seems that your provider may well be at fault.  My guess is Xitami is
working fine - as it is serving out web pages to those who can get to it.
Hopefully with enough experimentation, you'll find a port that everyone can
get through on.

And, I'm not trying to get on your case, cause I don't even care cause I'm
on high-speed and got drive space for weeks, but your original response to
my post that I received at 3:48 PM was in html - not the one you sent the
screen shot of.

Jay Aldrich

From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org] On Behalf Of Control-Freak
Sent: Wednesday, February 06, 2002 3:54 PM
To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Subject: Re: [Xitami] Linksys Router and Xitami


Hello Many Lists,

I'm sorry, but I thought you said:

> > > I have the exact same setup as you but it wont work for me.

1) You are not using Road Runner - you are using AT&T
2) You are not using dns2go, you are using some other name server
3) You are using a subdomain of a domain that is hosted in another state
- I have a single domain
4) Doesn't sound like your ip is dynamic, although it is not clear at
this point
5) You are using the xitami html interface,  while I am editing the
config files directly

The suggestions I gave in my last post was specific to my setup.  And,
yes, www is required in order to use port forwarding in dns2go.  I know
it is not required in general, but it is what the dns2go sever program
specifically looks for in order to know what to port forward and not
port forward.  In other words dns2go will not port forward
http://mydomain.com  , but it will port forward http://www.mydomain.com
.  It all ends up at the same ip, but only the one with the www prefix
gets port forwarded by dns2go (in other words its specific to dns2go).

I'm sorry but your setup is very different than mine.  From your
responses, it seems that your provider may well be at fault.  My guess
is Xitami is working fine - as it is serving out web pages to those who
can get to it. Hopefully with enough experimentation, you'll find a port
that everyone can get through on.

And, I'm not trying to get on your case, cause I don't even care cause
I'm on high-speed and got drive space for weeks, but your original
response to my post that I received at 3:48 PM was in html - not the one
you sent the screen shot of.

Jay Aldrich



--
Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami

If you are running windows and you want to see if you have an ip assigned
type winipcfg ... then disconnect and reconnect and do it again ... if the
ip remains the same a few days running then you have fixed ip if not its
dynamic.

If they were routing using mac addresses your laptop wouldn't work at all so
its tcp/ip.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb  8 00:08:56 2002

Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)

Absolutely not, you just have to ensure that

     1. the webuser has execute privileges in the cgi-bin directory
     2. points to the cgi executable
     3. Your cgi executable is reading it's stdin etc correctly

You may have to resort to pop up messages or text log files produced by your cgi
program to let you know if xitami is actually calling your executable.

Regards, Paul

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb  8 00:40:15 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Fri, 8 Feb 2002 10:40:15 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)
Message-ID: <4A256B5A.0003E129.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>


cgi-bin is a acronym for "Common GateWay Binary" directory. You can place any
executable in the directory and run it as long as the executable takes it's
input from stdin and environment variables and sends it's output to stdout. That
is you can write your own cgi exe's as long as you adhere to the published CGI
protocol.

Deplhi and C++Builder are good examples of development environments that are
delivered with the necessary components to create CGI binaries, many people use
third party libraries to write vb programs for cgi.

Perl and php are most commonly used because they transparently handle the CGI
protocol for you. However, if perl or php are used then the perl binary (it's
large) or php.exe have to be launched in order to interpret / compile the
script. Sometimes a small stand alone exe can perform far better under load.
It's a matter of trading convenience / performance.

For REALLY GOOD performance an LRWP is the answer with Xitami.

Paul

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb  8 06:43:01 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 08 Feb 2002 01:43:01 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)
References: <NFBBKNGGELNPLMHPBOCECEMNCHAA.admin@miplanet.net>
Message-ID: <3C637375.C4C2861C@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I have not seen anything run in the cgi-bin directory that wasn't a cgi or perl script, 

As Mr Shortis says, "CGI" is an interface between a web server
program and any other program. I don't think "a cgi" has much
meaning, except that it is probably -something- that can work
with the CGI protocol. 

>  I guess you could run about any exe file there. 

Yes. On a Windows machine, put Sol.exe in your cgi-bin folder. Go
to a browser on another machine and call
http://othermachine/cgi-bin/sol.exe. Nothing will happen in the
browser, it will time-out waiting for a reply; sol.exe is not
meant to read and write data according to the CGI protocol. But
when you go back to the server you will find Solitaire started
and ready to play. 

Which is a reason to be VERY careful what you put in the CGI
folder. Solitaire is pointless but safe (unless someone opens a
hundred copies of it and chokes the server RAM); but other
programs, especially ones that read and write to standard input
and output, can send back all sorts of information.

The testcgi.exe program that used to come with Xitami-Win is an
example. It shows anybody several bits of information about the
server machine's configuration, like PATH and where the HTTP
files are actually stored. In itself it isn't a lot of exposure,
but in conjunction with other info it could aid a hacker. 

BTW: in DOS/Win a BAT file can be a useful CGI program. It gets
awkward in a hurry (DOS BAT files eat "<" signs and aren't too
smart anyway) but I use a BAT file to call a filter and an
emailer  and a logger in sequence. In unix, shell-scripts can be
very useful CGI programs. (Also very dangerous because of the
power of the unix shell.)

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb  8 22:01:42 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 8 Feb 2002 17:01:42 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Wheres my cgi???
In-Reply-To: <aa.6400d0c.2995a2ad@aol.com>
References: <aa.6400d0c.2995a2ad@aol.com>
Message-ID: <66950990021.20020208170142@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I cant seem to find my cgi-bin!  Its supposed to be at
c:\xitami\cgi-bin but  its not there. ... the 'test cgi' thingie
doesnt work..

The demo CGI files that used to come with Xitami were not real
useful and might compromise security. The CGI files were removed
from the latest release; the package builder saw that the CGI-BIN
folder was empty so didn't include it at all.
  
> Can I create my own cgi-bin folder?

Absolutely.

If you have no handy CGI program to try, put this text in a file and
save it as .\cgi-bin\test.bat :

@echo Hello!

Then open http://localhost/cgi-bin/test.bat and it should say
"Hello!" at you.

 -PRR

In message <aa.6400d0c.2995a2ad@aol.com>, Marie180@aol.com writes:
>I have just downloaded and installed the xitami web server (windows 98).  I 
>cant seem to find my cgi-bin!  [...]
>Can I create my own cgi-bin folder?

Yes, please do.

The testcgi was left out of the base install over concerns that it was a
security risk (it does tell various details about your computer by
default); the cgi-bin directory was accidentally left out because there
was nothing in the directory (and the installer we use generally omits
empty directories).

Ewen

which they had responded.

problem"?

What is so difficult in <http://www.geocities.com/nnqweb/nquote.html>

At 09:22 AM 2/10/2002 -0500, raz writeth:
>   I want to disable the webserver and just use the  ftp daemon, how would
>I do that? 

Unfortunately, Xitami doesn't allow this as far as I can tell.  You could
try modifying the source.  Also, if you have firewall, you can just put the
HTTP server on a different port and block it at the firewall level and then
forward FTP to the proper port.

Hope this helps!

In message <006601c1b23e$71b81350$6501a8c0@raz>, "raz" writes:
>I want to disable the webserver and just use the ftp daemon, how would I =
>do that?

You can't.  Xitami is a webserver, which happens to have a small FTP add
on.  If you just want FTP you'd be better off using a different FTP
server.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Feb 10 23:56:31 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)

References: <006601c1b23e$71b81350$6501a8c0@raz>

> I want to disable the webserver and just use the ftp daemon

While I like Xitami's FTP module, it is hardly a full-featured
FTP server. And as Thomas said, it isn't meant to be run apart
from the HTTP server. 

There are LOTs of decent stand-alone FTP servers out there. Most
are more complete FTP machines than the Xitami module. 

See http://serverwatch.internet.com/ftpservers.html for a fairly
good listing. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb 13 19:35:04 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Viraf Mohta)
Date: Wed, 13 Feb 2002 14:35:04 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Intranet works, Internet doesn't
Message-ID: <FJELLPMKLMPKNOKMHGKFOEPECGAA.viraf_mohta@yahoo.com>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_000B_01C1B49B.A03A9950
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit


Hi there:

I am hoping someone on the list can shed some light on a problem I'm having
accessing my server from the Internet.

I have a network running at home (Win98SE, ICS, and Xitami), and am able to
get an HTTP response from Xitami on Port 9080 from within the network but
not from outside , i.e. the Internet. Here's the setup:

- Cable Internet connection. The cable provider has confirmed that it's
blocking Port 80.  Hence my server is running on Port 9080.

- The cable modem is connected to a Compaq 200 (w/164 MB RAM) running Win
98(SE), Microsoft ICS, and Xitami Ver. 2.4d9.

- This Compaq is connected to an 8-port hub which in turn provides Internet
access via ICS to 5 other machines on the home network.  This is also the
machine on which Xitami (Ver. 2.4d9) is installed (http on Port 9080).

All machines including the server can access the Internet and each other.
All machines including the server can successfully access Port 9080 from
within the network using all methods (Cable provided IP address,
192.168.0.1, 127.0.0.1, and computer name).  But I can't get Xitami to
respond from outside the network.  I assumed ZoneAlarm was causing this.  I
uninstalled it, but it didn't make a differnce.

Xitami is installed with the defaults, except that http is on port 9080, and
FTP on port 9121.  No other changes.

Can anyone offer any suggestions, please?

Thanks for taking the time to read this.

Regards,

Viraf

>Ewen-

Thanks.   It has turned up here now.

I've changed the list to be "members posting only".  

Anyone who has been posting from an address other than the one that they
are subscribed from should either (a) use the address they're subscribed
from for posting or, (b) subscribe the other address as well in a
"nomail" mode.  (What this means is that you'll be able to send mail
from both subscribed addresses, but the list will only send out copies
of the messages to one of the addresses.  This can be done from the
webpages.)

Ewen

This is off subject, but I reported the spam to the provider of the IP
address that the "click here" pointed to, and apparently the server has
been closed down just since this morning. 

I am working on a set of pages that show how to report spam to the
managing provider of the place the spam actually originated from. The
pages will also cover how to report to the provider if the spam came
through an open SMTP server or through a mailing list like this one did.
I have had very good results using this method.

The pages are still under development and probably won't be complete for
another couple of weeks, but some of the data is available now if anyone
is interested.

http://CowboyFrank.net/spam/index.htm
http://CowboyFrank.net/spam/mailclients.htm
http://CowboyFrank.net/spam/ascii.htm

References: <mVRXm+AhBva8EwNy@alan-lam.co.uk>

> The filter in xitami .php points to f:\internet\php

> test page  c:\my documents\alan\html\alan-lam\phptest.html

The ".php" filter only applies to files with a ".php" extension, but
your test file is called ".html".

The server returns the un-processed file. Because your example has
no visible elements, it looks blank.

Change that file's name to phptest.php and see what you get.

 -PRR

At 12:06 PM 2/14/2002 +1300, daniel carter writeth:
>So apparently running xitami in turbo mode will damage your hardware.

No, that's not what the article says.  The only way your hardware will be
damaged is if it runs in an uncirculated environment and the CPU overheats
or has electrical problems.  In either of those cases you have a more
fundamental problem than just Xitami.

There is nothing wrong with running Xitami in turbo mode.  However, as a
result of running it in turbo mode, it *will* skew benchmarking statistics
as it gets higher thread priority than both IIS and Apache.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb 13 19:27:59 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Wed, 13 Feb 2002 19:27:59
Subject: [Xitami] NT Services
In-Reply-To: <200202130033.BAA09633@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20020213192759.009e1238@shininglightpro.com>

At 04:24 PM 2/12/2002 -0800, Gunnar Swan writeth:
>	
> Good Day,
>
> Assume I run an uninstall on a service (which was shut down).
> The uninstall does not remove the service from the Control Panel.
> How can I remove this service. The EXE has gone away.
> I'm ending up with two services, one of which I disable (the old one I
want to go away)

Start a Command Prompt (Start->Run, type 'cmd', press enter).
Go to the Xitami directory:

C:\>_
C:\>cd progra~1\xitami

C:\PROGRA~1\Xitami>_

Now, launch Xitami and tell it to remove itself as a service:

C:\PROGRA~1\Xitami>xiwinnt -uninstall
Xitami web server v2.4d9 (c) 1991-99 iMatix
Xitami is free software and comes with ABSOLUTELY NO WARRANTY.
You may redistribute this software under certain conditions;
read the file COPYING for details.  Type xiwinnt -h for help.

xiwinnt: stopping service 'Xitami'... Ok
xiwinnt: service 'Xitami' removed

C:\PROGRA~1\Xitami>_

That's it!

Hope this helps!


          Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@shininglightpro.com
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb 13 22:48:51 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Wed, 13 Feb 2002 23:48:51 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Spam
Message-ID: <47078@dsl.co.uk>

In message <004b01c1b4dc$dffb07a0$6500a8c0@COWBOY>
   "Frank Harrell" writes:

> This is off subject, but I reported the spam to the provider of the IP
> address that the "click here" pointed to, and apparently the server has
> been closed down just since this morning. 

Well done; I *do* like confirmed kills :-)

> I am working on a set of pages that show how to report spam to the
> managing provider of the place the spam actually originated from. The
> pages will also cover how to report to the provider if the spam came
> through an open SMTP server or through a mailing list like this one did.

One of the biggest problems these days are computers running open SOCKS
proxies (often on ADSL or cable modems).  The owners of these machines
install such a proxy service to facilitate sharing a connection between
multiple computers in a home/SoHo, and take no steps to secure it against
being exploited by outsiders.

The latter come along and send their UCE ["spam" is the wrong
nomenclature] via the ISP's smart host, which is not an open SMTP relay,
but doesn effectively act as one, because it's been duped into believing
that the traffic has originated from an authorized user.

AIUI, the worst example of this for the Windoze world is something called
AnalogX, which comes with the SOCKS proxies completely open by default.
The manual does say how to close it down and make it secure, but...
how many people ever bother to RTFM, hey?

> I have had very good results using this method.

UCE/UBE is always worth fighting (if you just sweep it under the carpet
by filtering it, nothing will ever be done by ISPs to eradicate it at
source), but with the existence of things like AnalogX it becomes VERY
much harder to identify the real source.

-- 
Brian {Hamilton Kelly}                                          bhk@dsl.co.uk
    "We have gone from a world of concentrated knowledge and wisdom to one of
    distributed ignorance.  And we know and understand less while being incr-
    easingly capable."              Prof. Peter Cochrane, formerly of BT Labs

Content-type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"

I read the article Andreaz and as a systems programmer for many years I have
written many task schedulers.

It is a common misnomer that bad processes use more CPU time and that they can
damage a system. Let me set this straight...
this is total rubbish ! Any process that performs a lot of work is capable of
using 100% cpu time (even a simple calculation loop). The
real measure of an operating is how fairly is shares time amongst two CPU
intensive tasks (windows is not very good (read terrible)
in this regard.

In any case the only time the CPU time used by Xiami in turbo mode would be a
problem would be if you were using the same PC to
perform other tasks other than serving web pages. If it is a dedicated web
server run it in turbo mode and get the best performance
BECAUSE it will use as much available CPU time as it can.

Regards, Paul

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Feb 14 07:04:08 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 14 Feb 2002 20:04:08 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] SSI won't get data from another page?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Matt Fontaine" <Fontaine@Purdue.edu>
 of "Wed, 13 Feb 2002 12:59:43 CDT." <NFBBLAJNNACAPEPIMNLMEEMHCBAA.Fontaine@Purdue.edu>
Message-ID: <200202140704.UAA31737@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NFBBLAJNNACAPEPIMNLMEEMHCBAA.Fontaine@Purdue.edu>, "Matt Fontaine" writes:
>That didn't work - How can I specify to pull the text file from another web
>server?  It's not stored on this machine.  

In that case server-side-includes will not do what you want; it can
handle only files that are actually on your machine.

You'll need something to download the file from the remote machine
(fairly easy in Perl, Python, etc), and then either do that regularly
(eg, with a time-triggered program) or on demand (by using PHP or Perl
or something like that to process your pages).

You're welcome to try to change PerlSSI to do something like this,
but note that the Xitami 2.5 beta includes SSI support internally.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

You can't call a page from an other server using ssi but yo can use an
iframe or java script.

if you want to use these contact me and I'll walk you through it and show
you how.

and

demos=G:\site\demos (docs say "This section lets you define multiple CGI program roots")

I would like to set up multiple cgi directories.  I have done this using the CGI-Alias setting, like so:

[CGI-Alias]
abc=c:\web\abc\cgi-bin                 
xyz=c:\web\xyz\cgi-bin      

Now, this seems to work when I point my browser to http://localhost/abc/script.py and http://localhost/xyz/script.py, except that relative paths in the generated html are not resolved correctly: references to images at "../images/x.jpg" fail to find the file, and a style sheet link of "../file.css" fails to find the style sheet.  If I move the style sheet into the cgi-bin directory with the scripts and change the link to "file.css" in the html, it works fine.   Where is the server looking for the files that it can't find?  How can I get these relative paths to work?

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Feb 16 06:39:31 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 16 Feb 2002 19:39:31 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Crazy question
In-Reply-To: Message from "Alvaro E. Siman" <alsiman@cofs.net>
 of "Fri, 15 Feb 2002 22:56:19 CDT." <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCCECOCFAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <200202160639.TAA11112@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCCECOCFAA.alsiman@cofs.net>, "Alvaro E. Siman" writes:
>Can an Internet server, such as Xitami, pick up pages that are in an
>Intranet server in its network and serve them out to the Internet??

A proxy server can do this; Xitami doesn't currently have this
functionality (although you could add something like it with a CGI,
PHP/Perl, or a LRWP program.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

In message <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCCECOCFAA.alsiman@cofs.net>, "Alvaro E.
Siman" writes:
>Can an Internet server, such as Xitami, pick up pages that are in an
>Intranet server in its network and serve them out to the Internet??

A proxy server can do this; Xitami doesn't currently have this
functionality (although you could add something like it with a CGI,
PHP/Perl, or a LRWP program.

>Can Xitami behave as a proxy server to an IIS server?

No.  Because Xitami is not a proxy server (it doesn't have the necessary
functionality).  I've used both Apache and Squid (web caching software)
as proxy servers in the past; there may be others.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Feb 16 22:03:11 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Sat, 16 Feb 2002 23:03:11 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Crazy question
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCAEDACFAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <3C6ED71F.2050103@freesbee.fr>

Alvaro E. Siman wrote:

>Can Xitami behave as a proxy server to an IIS server?
>
No. If you need a proxy install squid. A linux box can quite successfuly 
be both a Xitami web server and a Squid proxy server. It can even (if 
you so desire) transparently proxy and run Xitami at the same time.

Although they get rather stroppy with people modifying the config 
because its really a firewall, smoothwall (www.smoothwall.org) is 
everything you need except the Xitami webserver.

Francis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Feb 17 18:54:43 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Alan Lam)
Date: Sun, 17 Feb 2002 18:54:43 +0000
Subject: [Xitami] Installing PHP4 with Win 98SE & Xitami v2.4d9
In-Reply-To: <001c01c1b6ec$f20fbfa0$0100a8c0@Patricko>
References: <wOU+nKAUDgb8Ew2t@alan-lam.co.uk>

Message-ID: <Rlka6jAzx$b8EwBY@alan-lam.co.uk>

>check your error.log file, cgierr.log also your phperror.log
>
>if you eneabled it and gave it a name in the php.ini file
>
>in your AUTOEXEC.BAT add this
>
>SET PATH=f:\internet;%PATH%

>NOTE the use of My documents has been known to give Xitami fits it don't
>like spaces :)
>
>hope this helps

To take out spaces
I've set up alias
temp=c:\temp


In autoexec.bat I've added
set path=f:\internet\php;%path%

I didn't know about the phperror.log. I downloaded the 'big' version of
php to have a look at the php.ini file. (I initially had the windows
installer version). I found out I can set display error!


The php.ini in the windows directory is now

; php.ini for PEAR tests
include_path=..

[mail function]
SMTP= localhost ; for Win32 only
sendmail_from= me@localhost.com ; for Win32 only

[Session]
session.save_path= F:\Internet\PHP\sessiondata    ; argument passed to
save_handler

[PHP]
error_reporting= E_ALL; display all errors, warnings and notices
display_errors = On
display_startup_errors = On
log_errors = On



With a test page
http://localhost/temp/Test Page.html
=>
http://localhost/temp/Test%20Page.html
and pops up fine.

With the php page

<html><head><title>PHP Test</title></head> 
<body> 
<?php echo "Hello World<P>"; ?> 
</body></html> 


http://localhost/temp/phptest.php

I see now see (with the help of display_error = on) :-)

Fatal error: Unable to open F:/Internet/Xitami/webpages/temp/phptest2.ph
p in Unknown on line 0


So ... where and what do I set to get php & xitami talking to each other
about the right directory?

Thanks
-- 
Alan YC Lam  Tonbridge, Kent, UK
email        alan@alan-lam.co.uk
www          http://www.alan-lam.co.uk

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Feb 17 22:52:41 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Mon, 18 Feb 2002 08:52:41 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] php+xitami
Message-ID: <4A256B63.007DE412.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>


create a file in one of your published web directories with an extension
of .php (I usually call it info.php) then place the following in it.

<?php
     phpinfo();
?>

Make sure you have set php.exe up as the filter to process files files with a
.php extension. Then point a browser at the url of the published file & you
should be rewarded with about 4 pages of html describing your php
configuration.

Good luck, Paul

Leave the filter at the setting that gives a blank page (single spashes) then
add the path to
php.exe/php4ts.dll to you PATH variable, the blank page usually means that
Xitami was able to
launch php.exe but for some reason php.exe was unable to load it's dll.
