From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Feb 18 02:37:21 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Many Lists)
Date: Sun, 17 Feb 2002 18:37:21 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] Crazy question
In-Reply-To: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCKEDDCFAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <000001c1b825$313c4a20$e82de00c@personal>

Q:Intel Cache Appliance racks on ebay go for about $300.00 nowadays.

Response: I didn't know that Intel made internet Caches. Could you send
me a link offline? Thanks

Q: "Is a cache appliance the same thing as a proxy server???"

A: As the name would suggest they are both different functions which are
often combined into the same device.
Internet Cache, Cache Appliance, Squid basically refer to a box which
sits at a connection before the internet.   If the WebPages are used
often the computer stores it on the hard drive, next time someone makes
a request to the internet it will check the box to see if a cached
version is there.   If it is, it saves time for the user and bandwidth
for the business & Isp. Which contrary to belief is not free. 

 A Proxy Server is essentially a gateway in which can perform specified
network functions. Most of the time when people refer to a proxy they
either want to a)use NAT Network Address Translation b)Restrict what
websites you can access or c)restrict or control bandwidth. (How much a
particular IP can download etc.)

http://www.webopedia.com/TERM/c/cache.html

http://www.webopedia.com/TERM/p/proxy_server.html

If you are a whiz at linux you could make a little box do your e-mail,
web server, nat and caching  very inexpensively.

Q:"Do they all have the capability of serving ASP (or other dynamic
pages) that are sitting behind them?"

A:  If you wish to know how a device would "serve" ASP pages then it
would also depend on the "web server" software that you choose.

Toodles

browser access to your web pages.

interchangably as if they were the same thing.

I take it a cache appliance can serve dynamic pages, since by definition
dynamic content cant be stored and re-served without a new query taking
place.

rest of the world is just lost.  Linux thumpers believe the rest of the
world are just lowly idiots that are nothing more than herded cattle being
led to slaughter.

Xitami is a web server that works on both Linux and Windows OSes, so like it
or not, there are gonna be quite a few Windows users on this list.  And even
though it isn't necessarily a good thing, Windows is still the most
popular/common OS on the planet.  And most of these Windows users who are
starting a Xitami-based web server for the first time, and are requesting
assistance, have not yet encountered the likes of a Linux thumper.  They
probably didn't even know that Outlook defaults to HTML messages.  And, they
surely had no idea that it was gonna piss someone off to no end if they did
unknowingly post in HTML.  Face it, HTML is gonna keep coming . . . .

go start their own list and call it

Don't sweat the small stuff in life.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Feb 18 15:33:09 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Alvaro E. Siman)
Date: Mon, 18 Feb 2002 10:33:09 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] List Filtering
In-Reply-To: <009901c1b836$ae315d20$b61e2341@concentric.net>
Message-ID: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCOEDGCFAA.alsiman@cofs.net>

About this whole Linux superiority complex:

1.) The internet is a visual medium, like it or not.  Most of these over
zealous Linux fans brush the reality of this off by saying that you can
create web pages with a simple text editor.  However true that may be, that
assumes that your web graphics are already made, and only need to be called
up.

Until you can run the full suite of Adobe products on Linux, then Linux is
useless as a web graphics platform.  No text editor replaces Adobe Photoshop
or Illustrator.  And if your answer to web graphics is colored text and font
manipulation........well, you just don't get what the Internet is doing.

The ideal environment for graphics is an Apple (considering that Silicon
Graphics machines are out of the reach of everyone who is not Lucasfilm and
Pixar).  Considering that Apple does not even have a server, much less a
database server or web server, they are quickly becoming uncomfortably
unconnected to the new breed of web designers.

This leaves Windows (Winblows to you Linux zealots) as a very attractive
option.  You don't need to know three operating systems, and you can even
stretch your machine to host both a Xitami server and have that same machine
create the graphics, create the web page, manage the web page.....and even
host a database.  Crazy, but if budget is an issue, you cant beat having a
minimum of software titles and a minimum of operating systems to learn and
deploy.

2.) I wont even get into the sound editing issue, since Linux does not even
exist in that field.  However, I will point out that sound IS PART OF the
multimedia realm.

3.) I guess you could pay a graphic designer $90.00 per hour if you want
your web pages to have more than just colored text and pasty
backgrounds........but, hey, that would defeat the whole "self-sufficiency"
of the Linux religion.

4.) Reading nasty messages is definitely much more distracting than simply
erasing a post that was sent using HTML mail.

So lay off the newbies....or simply go create the user group that someone
suggested below.  In order to keep the email list name shorter I suggest you
simply call it LINUX.  Everyone understands this term to be the synonym for
ONE DIMENSIONAL anyways.

P.S. --- Hey look ma!! I wrote this without using HTML!!!

> create a file in one of your published web directories with an extension
> of .php (I usually call it info.php) then place the following in it.
>
> <?php
>      phpinfo();
> ?>
>
> Make sure you have set php.exe up as the filter to process files files
with a
> .php extension. Then point a browser at the url of the published file &
you
> should be rewarded with about 4 pages of html describing your php
> configuration.
>
> Good luck, Paul

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 19 10:14:09 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Melle Koning)
Date: Tue, 19 Feb 2002 02:14:09 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [Xitami] LOG Filter to remove those log-entries created by http-viruses.
Message-ID: <20020219101409.38593.qmail@web9601.mail.yahoo.com>

Hello all,

To get rid of all the log-entries created by
http-viruses, I have created a little windows-program
that processes logfiles and removes those 'dirty'
log-entries that clogup the xitami-logfile.

You can view all removed lines and kept lines in the
program because all lines are copied in the listboxes.

You can download the program 'logfilter' at:
http://hace.dyndns.org/files/files.html

Please first read the logfilter.TXT file for further
comments.

If you have questions or suggestions for the program
please sent those to my email address.

Hope this helps people who where searching for this
kind of software and couldn't find it (like myself
;-),

Thanks,
Hace

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 19 15:40:41 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 19 Feb 2002 10:40:41 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Vhosts?
In-Reply-To: <002501c1b8e1$22b4a120$0101a8c0@AdrianMoore>
References: <002501c1b8e1$22b4a120$0101a8c0@AdrianMoore>
Message-ID: <1391878286433.20020219104041@rci.rutgers.edu>

> catch all requests from a given adress (http://site_x.com) and
> direct it to a specific folder on the web server.

_FROM_ a specific address, or TO ?

By default, a web server will serve any request that comes to it. If
you have many DNS names all pointed to the same physical
machine/server (same IP or a milti-IP machine), and leave Vhost
alone, all requests to any name of the machine will get the
specified folder.

If you want requests to certain names to get different folders, then
you use Vhosts.

If you want a request FROM "joe.q.public.com to see
"/wwwfiles/public", but a request from "adrian.insider.com" to see
"/wwwfiles/insiders"....  Xitami won't do that, make decisions based
on the viewer's hostname. You could do something with PHP, or a
fancy firewall.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 19 20:36:31 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 20 Feb 2002 09:36:31 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Implizit frameset?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Robert M. Muench" <robert.muench@robertmuench.de>
 of "Tue, 19 Feb 2002 20:49:56 BST." <NCBBLHNNKNPMOBPMIBDHMEOBOMAA.robert.muench@robertmuench.de>
Message-ID: <200202192036.JAA13342@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NCBBLHNNKNPMOBPMIBDHMEOBOMAA.robert.muench@robertmuench.de>, "Robert
 M. Muench" writes:
>And now there is a root-document that performs a check for frames and loads the
>given URL inside a frame. Why this? Where does this document come from?
>
>IMO Xitami must be issuing it automatically?

It's not Xitami issuing it automatically; Xitami doesn't know anything
about frames, and the only HTML that it includes/generates automatically
is _very_ basic for directory lists and error messages.

I'd say it's going to be something in the website files that you put in.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 19 20:55:53 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 19 Feb 2002 15:55:53 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Problems accessing internal IP address
In-Reply-To: <FJELLPMKLMPKNOKMHGKFMEBDCHAA.viraf_mohta@yahoo.com>
References: <FJELLPMKLMPKNOKMHGKFMEBDCHAA.viraf_mohta@yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <1241897198607.20020219155553@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  It works from WITHIN the network, but not if I try this
from outside.

Internal IP numbers SHOULDN'T work from "the outside".

Does the other machine have an external IP number or name? If not
(and typically small networks won't), then nobody outside will ever
see it.

 -PRR


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 19 21:05:15 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gerry Aquino)
Date: Tue, 19 Feb 2002 15:05:15 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] Problems accessing internal IP address
In-Reply-To: <FJELLPMKLMPKNOKMHGKFMEBDCHAA.viraf_mohta@yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <web-410364@sesslerford.com>

I dont't think you will be able to "get to" 192.168.0.50 
from the internet as this is a private non-routable ip 
address. I also don't think this is a Xitami problem. My 
guess is that you would have to define a directory alias 
for your external path or just use another port from your 
24.190.xxx.xxx address forwarded to the 192.168.0.50 
machine. For example use 24.190.xx.xxx:9090 forwarded to 
192.168.0.50. HTH

-gerry

  >>> hace_x@yahoo.com 02/19/02 04:14AM >>>
  Hello all,

  To get rid of all the log-entries created by
  http-viruses, I have created a little windows-program
  that processes logfiles and removes those 'dirty'
  log-entries that clogup the xitami-logfile.

  You can view all removed lines and kept lines in the
  program because all lines are copied in the listboxes.

  You can download the program 'logfilter' at:
  http://hace.dyndns.org/files/files.html

  Please first read the logfilter.TXT file for further
  comments.

  If you have questions or suggestions for the program
  please sent those to my email address.

  Hope this helps people who where searching for this
  kind of software and couldn't find it (like myself
  ;-),

  Thanks,
  Hace

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 19 23:09:32 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)

> Any ideas what they are trying to do? I have noticed them on and
>off for several weeks now.

CodeRed and Nimda have been flogging the internet for months.

The very-very long request causes an overflow in some web servers.
The intended target is unpatched MS IIS. On that server, the
overflow writes on program space. The little bit of goblygook at the
end is CPU code that "is" the virus.

They also make some other servers unhappy, but because they don't
have the same program code in the same spot they don't get infected.
Just maybe crash.

Xitami is quite immune to the CodeRed exploit. Its writers assumed
that requests might have garbage in them and don't let requests
overflow into program space.

>All trying to hit port 8888

Very odd, it is usually port 80. Maybe a new variant hoping to hit
all you guys behind ISPs that block 80.

 -PRR

----- Original Message -----
From: "Paul Reid" <preid@rci.rutgers.edu>
To: "Adrian C. Moore" <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Tuesday, February 19, 2002 7:40 AM
Subject: Re: [Xitami] Vhosts?


> > catch all requests from a given adress (http://site_x.com) and
> > direct it to a specific folder on the web server.
>
> _FROM_ a specific address, or TO ?
>
> By default, a web server will serve any request that comes to it. If
> you have many DNS names all pointed to the same physical
> machine/server (same IP or a milti-IP machine), and leave Vhost
> alone, all requests to any name of the machine will get the
> specified folder.
>
> If you want requests to certain names to get different folders, then
> you use Vhosts.
>
> If you want a request FROM "joe.q.public.com to see
> "/wwwfiles/public", but a request from "adrian.insider.com" to see
> "/wwwfiles/insiders"....  Xitami won't do that, make decisions based
> on the viewer's hostname. You could do something with PHP, or a
> fancy firewall.
>
>  -PRR
>
>
> --
> Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
> To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami
>

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 19 23:39:04 2002

Date: Tue, 19 Feb 2002 16:39:04 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Problems accessing internal IP address
References: <FJELLPMKLMPKNOKMHGKFMEBDCHAA.viraf_mohta@yahoo.com> <1241897198607.20020219155553@rci.rutgers.edu> <OE699gPF0R572DAzo7O00020f37@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <004301c1b99e$9e343f00$0b46dacf@rivcom.net>

The 192.168.0.50 address is not routable to an outside address. You would
need to do an internal routing through an external port to get there. For
instance port 9080.

David Holm <david.holm@rivcom.net>
System Administrator, River Communications

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 19 23:56:54 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 19 Feb 2002 18:56:54 -0500
Subject: Re[2]: [Xitami] Vhosts?
In-Reply-To: <004301c1b99d$51470f20$8f13a540@AdrianMoore>
References: <002501c1b8e1$22b4a120$0101a8c0@AdrianMoore>
 <1391878286433.20020219104041@rci.rutgers.edu>
 <004301c1b99d$51470f20$8f13a540@AdrianMoore>
Message-ID: <41908059143.20020219185654@rci.rutgers.edu>

> if I have two names set up at say dyndns.  one named
> frusterated.dyndns.com, and need-school.dyndns.com can I set up
> xitami to use a different vhost for each site?

Yes.

Open myserver.org/admin, click Vhost Wizard.

Click NEW in top left.

"Create virtual host profile:" [frusterated ].cfg

" enter DNS host name:" [frusterated.dyndns.com ]

"Web page root directory:" [ /frusterated  ]

"Create directories if necessary?" [X]

Click CREATE at bottom.

Do again for "need-school.dyndns.com".

Wait a few minutes. Or restart Xitami. Or restart Windows. Sometimes
Xitami seems reluctant to pick up new Vhosts, so don't panic too
fast.

I assume you already have frusterated.dyndns.com registered at a DNS
server such as dyndns.com . Won't work until that happens.

BTW: "frusterated" is not spelled the way I find in a dictionary.
They like "frustrated". Does not matter in URLs, and I know you are
just throwing out an example.

 -PRR

No you don't have to worry about those lines in your

your diskspace or make it more difficult for
analog-analyzers like analog (www.analog.cx).

the rubbish so created the logfilter.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb 20 11:27:54 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Wed, 20 Feb 2002 12:27:54 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami bug with relative redirects
Message-ID: <3C73883A.1050406@freesbee.fr>

Using the standard CGI.pm you can (theoretically) redirect people to a 
URl doing something like
print $query->redirect("destination.url"). This prints two lines to STDOUT

Status: 302 Moved
location: destination.url

And normally you get a redirect from there.

It works is my destination.url is a fully defined 
http://host/path/file.html or similar

But I have found 2 bugs in this with Xitami when one uses a non absolute URL

with a file only relative url (just file.html) it chops of the leading 
character to produce a redirect to ile.html in the ROOT of the webserver 
. i.e. the absolute URL is http://host/ile.html
with a path and file relative url (/path/file.html) the redirect never 
completes and xitami just sits there serving up nothing until you hit 
cancel - conceivably there is a timeout after 120 seconds or whatever 
but I didn't wait that long.

This does not appear to occur with Apache which handles both relative 
URLs just fine. Arguably this is a bug with the redirect generator as  
RFC 2616 (http 1.1) section 14.30 states that only absolute URIs are 
allowed for the location field, but it would be nice to see it 
documented if not fixed.

14.30 Location

   The Location response-header field is used to redirect the recipient
   to a location other than the Request-URI for completion of the
   request or identification of a new resource. For 201 (Created)
   responses, the Location is that of the new resource which was created
   by the request. For 3xx responses, the location SHOULD indicate the
   server's preferred URI for automatic redirection to the resource. The
   field value consists of a single absolute URI.


Francis

Air Force base, and shot.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Feb 21 21:12:06 2002

Subject: [Xitami] Fwd: Xitami, PHP and mySQL
Message-ID: <200202212121.WAA31637@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

Solved my own problem.
mysql on NT defaults to named pipes .... <<--- el stupido !!!

( Todo: set mysql to use tcpip on NT)  

Went with new ODBC driver for MySQL, and avoided internal libraries.
Temporarily set ODBC to use named pipes.  (NT !!!!)

Installed adodb for PHP  at http://php.weblogs.com/ADOdb
Problem solved.

Hi Russell,

Check the xitami logs and see if there is an error in there.

Remember that a lot of changes don't take effect till you reboot ...this =
means on a machine that runs for long periods, that changes made last =
week don't occur till this week when you reboot.

The vitamin log should tell you if there is an xitami start problem and =
what it is.

Garry Stanley

Cable.net.nz

 From Microsoft Support site----

Error 2140 When Starting Service With Parameters (Q136711)

 From the The following message appears when you attempt 
to manually start a service from Control Panel Services by 
selecting the service and specifying values in the Startup 
Parameters field: 


Could not start the <service_name> service on 
\\<server_name>. 
Error 2140: An internal Windows NT error occurred. 

Are you sure that IIS is not already running on port 80 
when you try to restart Xitami and thus the error??

just a thought..

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb 22 00:46:06 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Fri, 22 Feb 2002 10:46:06 +1000

--0__=jC3H9RUWByPOqymLSVkBQScyYBgniPU88i8QTXT0H0Nsj7aqPip9HW0X
Content-type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"
Content-Disposition: inline



Hi Russel,

I seem to recall having a similar problem some time ago when I was evaluating
Apache and Xitami on a server that also had IIS installed. You must ensure that
both IIS and the IIS Admin service are stopped.

My problem turned out to be that another process was already using one of the
ports required by my Xitami configuration. Try using "netstat -a -n" and
'netstat -a' to see if something else is already using port 80 etc.

Paul




Well, I completely uninstalled Xitami, removed it as a service, reboot the
Server and then reinstalled Xitami as a service again.  Still no luck - getting
the same "Error 2140".

Does Xitami use any files from the IIS Admin service? or from the FTP publishing
or the WWW Publishing (all parts of the IIS) - I currently don't have it
running.  An odd thing did occur: when Xitami didn't start (the first time all
these problems began), the IIS webserver did start.  Thats never happened before
- I do know those services were on manual so I am baffled as to how they
started.

I have done all the basic things and yet I can't get my Xitami service started.

HELP HELP HELP.  Don't know what to do here.

-R

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb 22 00:50:11 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 22 Feb 2002 13:50:11 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] HELP: NT/Xitami Server error.
In-Reply-To: Message from "Russel Olinger" <rolinger@airpower.net>
 of "Thu, 21 Feb 2002 16:16:04 -0800." <034301c1bb36$1f35eb60$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <200202220050.NAA29272@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <034301c1bb36$1f35eb60$020aa8c0@Master>, "Russel Olinger" writes:
>Does Xitami use any files from the IIS Admin service? or from the FTP =
>publishing or the WWW Publishing (all parts of the IIS)

No it doesn't.  

But if you have IIS installed and Xitami installed, both with their
default configuration they won't both run at once.  (Both try to be the
"default webserver" and there can be only one.)  Try ensuring that IIS
is _not_ running and then start Xitami.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

either.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb 22 01:35:33 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Russel Olinger)
Date: Thu, 21 Feb 2002 17:35:33 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] HELP: NT/Xitami Server error. FIXED!!!
References: <200202220050.NAA29272@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz> <039801c1bb3d$58c59ef0$020aa8c0@Master> <03b401c1bb3e$d5773390$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <03ba01c1bb41$387589e0$020aa8c0@Master>

kewl, rebuilding the config file took two seconds....Xitami discovers the
individual *.cfg files for each domain.  So after wiping out the
defaults.cfg and then going to the browser based admin page, Xitami still
saw all my different domains.  All I had to do was recopy the Xitami.cfg
file over to a new version of the defaults.cfg file and then edit the VH
section.  17 individual lines and its all back online now.

I never had to go through these processes before so some of the above
revelations you guys have probably already had - first time for me.

-Russel

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb 22 03:26:25 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 22 Feb 2002 16:26:25 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] HELP: NT/Xitami Server error.
In-Reply-To: Message from "Russel Olinger" <rolinger@airpower.net>
 of "Thu, 21 Feb 2002 17:07:49 -0800." <039801c1bb3d$58c59ef0$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <200202220326.QAA29805@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <039801c1bb3d$58c59ef0$020aa8c0@Master>, "Russel Olinger" writes:
>In what order do the files load.  Does Xitami.cfg load as well as
>defaults.cfg?  Or does only the defaults.cfg load.  

xitami.cfg loads defaults.cfg, and defaults.cfg generally loads your
virtual hosts, etc.  I'd definitely suggest looking in the error logs
for Xitami to see if you can find the reason it won't load -- xitami.log
is probably the most useful one to start with.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

On Friday 22 February 2002 03:24 am, you wrote:
> How can I run Xitami in a boot up time with init-script? My system is
> Mandrake 8.1. Xitami is installed in /var/xitami.

This is what I did for my Mandrake 8.1 system,
put this in /etc/rc.d/rc.local:

echo "Starting xitami"
/var/xitami/xitami -s -w /var/xitami
#Syntax: xitami [options...]
#Options:
#  -w directory     Working directory for server
#  -r directory     Root directory for web pages (webpages)
#  -c directory     Directory for CGI programs (cgi-bin)
#  -b portbase      Shift HTTP port 80 by this value.  E.g. to run
#                   Xitami on port 5080, do 'xitami -b 5000'
#  -f directory     Root directory for FTP files (webpages)
#  -q               Quiet mode: no messages
#  -s               Server mode: run as background job
#  -S               Console mode: run as foreground job
#  -t               Trace all socket i/o operations to log file
#  -v               Show Xitami version information
#  -h               Show summary of command-line options

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb 22 12:50:22 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 23 Feb 2002 01:50:22 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Newbie question - permissions under Win 98
In-Reply-To: Message from "Jim Scullion" <j.scullion@ayrcoll.ac.uk>
 of "Fri, 22 Feb 2002 11:47:26 -0000." <NGBBLLHPELKGGCABCJJNIEDHCAAA.j.scullion@ayrcoll.ac.uk>
Message-ID: <200202221250.BAA31900@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NGBBLLHPELKGGCABCJJNIEDHCAAA.j.scullion@ayrcoll.ac.uk>, "Jim Scullion" writes:
>I'm running Xitami under Windows 98, and I'd like to be able to change the
>permissions for cgi scripts etc.  I know that the Unix Chmod command does
>this.  How can it be done in a Windows environment?

It can't.  Windows 98 doesn't have any notion of "executable" in the
same way that unix systems do.  Instead anything that is *.exe, *.com,
*.bat, etc is considered executable.  Xitami also considers any script
that starts with a "#! interpreter" type line in a cgi-bin directory to
be executable.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb 22 16:04:05 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Gunnar Swan)
Date: Fri, 22 Feb 2002 08:04:05 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] HELP: NT/Xitami Server error.
Message-ID: <200202221612.RAA19495@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

If you uninstalled and reinstalled Xitami, go back to the folder
and make sure that the Xitami NT Service account under
which Xitami runs ... has read and write permissions to
/Xitami/ and all child folders.
Furthermore, if PHP is installed, the /PHP/ folder has to 
have the same NT account permissions as does the Xitami
folder.


2/21/02 4:50:11 PM, Ewen McNeill <ewen@imatix.com> wrote:

>In message <034301c1bb36$1f35eb60$020aa8c0@Master>, "Russel Olinger" writes:
>>Does Xitami use any files from the IIS Admin service? or from the FTP =
>>publishing or the WWW Publishing (all parts of the IIS)
>
>No it doesn't.  
>
>But if you have IIS installed and Xitami installed, both with their
>default configuration they won't both run at once.  (Both try to be the
>"default webserver" and there can be only one.)  Try ensuring that IIS
>is _not_ running and then start Xitami.
>
>Ewen
>

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Feb 22 23:53:33 2002

You are aware of the [Filter] section in the defaults.cfg.
You may have to set c:\PHP in your path too.
On NT, assign the same NT account to the Xitami folder, the NT service 
and PHP folder.

I don't think too many people are going to give you a hard time about
setup stuff. This is a pretty easy going list ...

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Feb 24 15:14:53 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (TCD Support)
Date: Sun, 24 Feb 2002 10:14:53 -0500 (Eastern Standard Time)
Subject: [Xitami] DNS
References: <002301c1bd0e$6bcbe180$542de00c@personal>
Message-ID: <3C79036D.000001.02220@work4>

DNS server software for Windows 95/98/ME does not exist in a true DNS server
form.  You need NT/2000/XP to run a proper DNS server.  There are some
software packages such as Simple DNS that you can use under 95/98/me, but it
is NOT a true DNS server. 
Linux/Unix is still the best and they are FREEWARE.  Try FreeBSD or Mandrake

Date: Sun, 24 Feb 2002 15:51:03 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] PHP Under Xitami
References: <3C790414.000007.02220@work4>
Message-ID: <004501c1bd74$f92cbfc0$325cfea9@cometstream>

first you need to download and install php
http://www.php.net/downloads.php

next open the 'defaults.cfg'  file under the 'Xitami' folder and add

[Filter]
    .php = "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"
    .php3 = "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"
    .phtml = "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"

NOTE: I'm on windows 98

-----Original Message-----
From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org

To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
Subject: Re: [Xitami] DNS



DNS server software for Windows 95/98/ME does not exist in a true DNS
server form.  You need NT/2000/XP to run a proper DNS server.  There are
some software packages such as Simple DNS that you can use under
95/98/me, but it is NOT a true DNS server. 
Linux/Unix is still the best and they are FREEWARE.  Try FreeBSD or
Mandrake

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Feb 24 21:44:59 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Alvaro E. Siman)
Date: Sun, 24 Feb 2002 16:44:59 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] DNS
In-Reply-To: <200202242127.WAA05588@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>
Message-ID: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCEEEMCFAA.alsiman@cofs.net>

Using your ISP's DNS IP's is great for surfing the web.  But that doesnt get
a domain name pointed to your web server's IP address.

If you want to point www.YourDomain.com to your domain server you will need
either a DNS server, or a DNS service.

DNS services are popping up everywhere.  My domain name registrar just
started offering the service just a little while ago.

Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="us-ascii"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

I am on a dynamic ip address, using dns2go to direct domain request to the
IP of my router. The router forwards to the SimpleDNS IP which translates
the request to an internal IP address for each domain. Right now I have 10
sites on 10 ip addresses and email hosting too. I have been using SimpleDNS
the whole time with out any problems. Now if there is another way to do it
without using a DNS server that's ok too. But the question was whether or
not there is a free or shareware DNS server out there and we answered that
question. Whether or not it's the best thing to use is another question
altogether.

And for all you Linux/Unix users, some of us just have never learned it so
it's not an option.

Sorry for the venting......

Ron

BulkRegister.com is my registrar.  I have over 300 domains with them.  Their
service isnt spectacular, but it is there and you do get call backs and
answers one or two days afterwards.

They have an initial membership fee, but if you are going to transfer or
register more than 10 domains it makes up for itself.

I have not used their DNS service, but it is available.  It wasnt a year ago
when I started using JHSoft's Simple DNS.

The only drawback of Simple DNS is that their tech support team has gone
awol in the last few months.  They used to answer within the hour.  Now they
dont answer at all.

open the 'defaults.cfg'  file under the 'Xitami' folder and add

[Filter]
    .php =3D "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"
    .php3 =3D "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"
    .phtml =3D "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 26 09:03:18 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ke Thoi)
Date: Tue, 26 Feb 2002 02:03:18 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] custom error
In-Reply-To: <200202260802.VAA02995@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <NEBBIJCGMNPMOJGCJHMGOEGMDGAA.xitami@i602.com>

I figured it out that apache actually "forwards" to an HTML page instead of
generating one. That's why it worked even with "friendly error messages"
checked. Any way this can be done with Xitami? So that it forwards to a
valid HTML page, so IE never knows it didn't exist? I found out that the
friendly error IS by default checked off... so majority of the people will
never see the custom message. Thanks for the help, that was insightful. Ke

I do not know because I do not use it but it should be the same thing

[Filter]
    .php =3D "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"
    .php3 =3D "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"
    .phtml =3D "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"
    .asp =3D "C:\\path\\to\\asp"             <<<<
  ----- Original Message -----=20
  From: Ken Than=20
  To: xitami@lists.xitami.org=20
  Sent: Tuesday, February 26, 2002 12:51 AM

    ----- Original Message -----=20
    From: Edward Williams=20

    open the 'defaults.cfg'  file under the 'Xitami' folder and add

    [Filter]
        .php =3D "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"
        .php3 =3D "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"
        .phtml =3D "C:\\PHP\\php.exe"

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 26 12:34:33 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Tue, 26 Feb 2002 13:34:33 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Aliases and PHP
References: <NEBBLGOJIKOELEDFHCCAEEBOEBAA.jhadfiel@oldihc.org>

Jim Hadfield wrote:

>Alan is right.
>I've been watching this closely for someone to respond.  I have had the
>problem on my system, but never had time to sit down to try and figure it
>out.
>
>Although, I will not be installing Apache.  I like Xitami too much.
>

There is a Xitami bug about case sensitivity and aliases which I have 
found. This could be related perhaps? The problem I have found is that 
if your OS is filename case sensitive (e.g. Linux) then you are hosed 
because the alias detection code goes and lowercases the path and the 
alias to check for a match.

I don't used PHP so I can't say whats wrong there but I will say that 
the Xitami alias matching code is perhaps not the best written part of 
Xitami. If you downlaod the source code then perhaps you can figure out 
what the difference is.

Francis

I think it's PHP&MYSQL problem.
Check up following:
1). Version PHP. If PHP is older than 4.0.5 that is necessary for extension " php_mysql.dll " (read PHP install.txt). In any case it is necessary to customize PHP (php.ini).
2). If You have FireWall, open access to MYSQL servera  ports.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Feb 26 20:18:34 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Fabian Bess)
Date: Tue, 26 Feb 2002 21:18:34 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Aliases and PHP
References: <NEBBLGOJIKOELEDFHCCAIEBPEBAA.jhadfiel@oldihc.org> <3C7B8BC5.4030902@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <3C7BED9A.8060200@gmx.net>

AFAIK, Xitami passes the .php-file which is to "execute" directly to the 
php.exe as a command line parameter and simply returns the output.
This problem is known for some time, though (several month), and there 
has not been any real workaround. If you are forced to use aliases bad luck.
I solved the problem by using virtual name-based hosts instead of 
aliased directories if the files are i.e. located on a file server. This 
works fine (as long as you won't use aliases below the virtual hosts 
level, of course ;-) ).
So the problem seems to be in the alias codepart of Xitami so that it 
won't handle any files which are to be passed to a program (i.e. filter 
like php.exe) correctly. I didn't try if perlssi or any other filter 
works because php is the only filter I'm using.

Greets

-- 
Fabian Bess (webmaster@tannenhof.de)
Webmaster Drogenhilfe Tannenhof Berlin e.V. 'http://www.tannenhof.de'

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Feb 27 00:22:14 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Alvaro E. Siman)
Date: Tue, 26 Feb 2002 19:22:14 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Frontpage Extensions without IIS
In-Reply-To: <000e01c1bedc$b2626540$542de00c@MWGXP>
Message-ID: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCOEFFCFAA.alsiman@cofs.net>

The last time the Xitami authors answered this question they said that they
had no intentions of reverse engineering to accomodate Microsoft's
propriatary work.

I think you can use the "Publish" feature of Front Page to put up the web
site and the subsequent versions.  This is no different than uploading
through an FTP connection, like Macromedia Dreamweaver uses to publish.

What you wont be able to do is manage the live site.  You wont be able to
log on with Front Page and browse the live folders in a Xitami web site, and
use Front Page's many management features.

You also wont be able to apply their "Themes", which make a lot of the
tedious formating work go away.  If you know CSS then this is not a problem.

This is actually a blessing in disguise: Macromedia has the right approach:
You should never fiddle with the live site.  You should only update the
latest version after testing the changes locally.

Also, Cascading Style Sheets make your site easier to manage than Front Page
extensions.  As long as you know CSS and HTML well enough, you are better
off than using Front Page's formating features.

YOU SAID:


I few years back I bought a Linux distribution which had the option of
loading FrontPage Extensions on it. Since Linux runs on so many Internet
servers perhaps giving that portion away for free was a way that
Microsoft could get into the market?

If it was not just for MS how could one load FP extensions for Xitami?

Thanks

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Feb 28 16:42:16 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ervin Kosch)
Date: Thu, 28 Feb 2002 11:42:16 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Re: StarOffice ADABAS with Dreamweaver UltraDev and Xitami
Message-ID: <000501c1c076$e26617a0$f7dea8c0@lmgonline.net>

Yes, but you have to use a scripting language like PHP or Cold Fusion(with
XiFusion).

If you want to use PHP you have to have PHAkt loaded into UltraDEV.

You'll have to use an ODBC connection language to use both languages since
neither language directly supports StarOffice ADABAS.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Feb 28 16:51:27 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Dmitry Isakbayev)
Date: Thu, 28 Feb 2002 11:51:27 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Keep Alive Max counter does not get decremented
Message-ID: <NEBBIJGPHKNLMOCJIHFJOECODAAA.dmitry@transnexus.com>

We are using "SSL/Pro Web Server v2.5b4".

Given these values in the defaults.cfg file -

[Server]
    keep-alive=1
    keep-alive-max=200
    timeout=3600


In the HTTP headers, "max" is always 200.  Is this a (known) problem?


It seems like "http_refresh_context" always resets "p_http->keep_alive_max"
to the configured value.

After making a few add-hoc changes -

1) removed call to "http_refresh_context" from
"smthttp.c::resolve_virtual_hostname"
2) removed call to "http_refresh_context" from
"smthttpl.c::http_init_context"
3) added   call to "http_refresh_context" to
"smthttp.c::initialise_the_thread" (right after calling "http_init_context")

"max" starts to get decremented for every response on the alive connection.

Thank You,

Dmitry

Seeing as lots of people using Xitami run PHP I thought the list might 
be interested in this

http://security.e-matters.de/advisories/012002.html

Advisory 01/2002
PHP remote vulnerabilities
 
 
 
*Release Date:* 2002/02/27
*Author:* Stefan Esser [s.esser@ematters.de] <mailto:s.esser@e-matters.de>
*Application:* PHP v3.0.10-v3.0.18, v4.0.1-v4.1.1
*Severity:* Several vulnerabilities in PHP's fileupload code allow 
remote compromise
*Risk:* Critical
*Reference:* http://security.e-matters.de/advisories/012002.html 
<http://security.e-matters.de/advisories/012002.html?SID=a87c7ca04ea241641a0aba3c4d52894f> 

*Last Modified:  * 2002/02/28

 
 
 
 
*Overview*

We found several flaws in the way PHP handles multipart/form-data POST 
requests. Each of the flaws could allow an attacker to execute arbitrary 
code on the victim's system.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Feb 28 19:03:31 2002

Hello Folks,

I do not know if this question has been asked before, searches found no answers so I thought I would ask.

When you create a virtual host and have it completly setup, how does one deligate administration of that virtual host to the site
owner ?

What we would like to do is allow folks that "own" those virtually hosted sites, manage it themselves for adding, removing users,
and protecting pages.

Any help in this matter would greatly be appreciated.

Thanks for time,
Roberto

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Feb 28 19:11:39 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (jay way)
Date: Thu, 28 Feb 2002 11:11:39 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] help needed re: setup of xitami using SMC NAT router/firewall
Message-ID: <JECOHGFBNNNGAAAA@shared1-mail.whowhere.com>

hello

i subscribed to the mailing list of xitami and have been reading the various posts now for a week and haven't seen any newbies posting a problem that i have...

i am currently running a win2k pro with SMC firewall/4 port switch/router that has net address translation capability.  when i recently installed the free xitami ver 2.5b5, i noticed that it has auto detected my internally assigned ip 192.168.2.77 and the recursive 127.0.0.1 ip.... i suspect that the reason that i cannot get the program to work properly is because i cannot find a place where i can enter my WAN ip or to let the program recognize a new ip...

or am i on the wrong track?

any help would be greatly appreciated...

jay

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Feb 28 20:57:10 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 01 Mar 2002 09:57:10 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] administration
In-Reply-To: Message from "Roberto R. Morelli" <morelli@altair7.com>
 of "Thu, 28 Feb 2002 11:03:31 -0800." <3C7E7F03.9485BD28@altair7.com>
Message-ID: <200202282057.JAA27123@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3C7E7F03.9485BD28@altair7.com>, "Roberto R. Morelli" writes:
>When you create a virtual host and have it completly setup, how does one 
>deligate administration of that virtual host to the site owner ?

One doesn't.  There's no concept of "virtual site ownership" in Xitami;
the system administrator owns them all.  You can set up FTP accounts so
that other people can upload files to the directories used by a given
virtual host, but that is about as close as it gets.  (With some
trickery you could let them edit the virtual host configuration files in
an editor and upload them like this, but this would probably be a
security risk too.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Feb 28 22:01:13 2002
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Mike McDaniel)
Date: Thu, 28 Feb 2002 17:01:13 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] help needed re: setup of xitami using SMC NAT router/firewall
References: <JECOHGFBNNNGAAAA@shared1-mail.whowhere.com>
Message-ID: <018f01c1c0a3$7222a580$6401a8c0@configxp>

Go into the router's IP forwarding tab and set tcp ports 80 and 21 for
192.168.2.77.
